Global Trends and Their Impact on Commodity Management

Volatility fueled by market dynamics

Increasing demand in emerging markets (China and India) 
is creating a tight balance between supply-and-demand 
Geopolitical uncertainties and the increasing influence of 
hedge funds and financial institutions

Increasing focus on Risk Management

Increased focus on risk management by crisis-shaken 
executives, driven by the need to protect earnings and keep 
company operations running

Compliance with government regulations like the 
Sarbanes-Oxley Act

Companies are struggling to keep up and comply with 
regulations like hedge accounting laws 
Strong demand for business solutions designed to meet 
these requirements

Volatile prices: Commodity prices keep changing, with little relief in sight.

Commodity Radar issued monthly by Commerzbank & Wirtschaftswoche.
The Commodity Radar shows that the volatility of commodities has been significant across all 
commodities from Industrial Metals, Precious Metals, Agricultural Commodities to Energy.
This trend is increasing.
What is also interesting is the comparison between the volatility of the various commodities 
and the volatility of interest rates and the Euro/Dollar exchange rate. Most companies today 
still focus their hedging activities on interest rates and foreign currencies. However, the impact 
commodity volatility has on profitability will often be much higher for companies producing or 
consuming large amounts of commodities. For these companies, understanding their 
exposure to commodity price volatility and thus being able to hedge this risk appropriately is of 
significant value.

Commodity Management Industries and Their Different 
Business Requirements

Cookie Producer is looking to manage their risk from procuring wheat for cookie 
production. Their business strategy is to be fully hedged.

Metal Smelter is looking to manage the price risk from buying in 
metal concentrates from their vendors and matching it against their 
sales contracts for finished metals. Their business strategy is to be 
fully hedged.

Large Can Producer is looking to manage their price risk from 
buying in aluminum. Their business strategy is to extract profits 
from trading aluminum based on their market and operational 
knowledge of aluminum.

Large Oil Producer is looking to trade their different products globally. Their 
business strategy is to maximize their profits through their trading operations 
and asset optimization.

Copper Grade A -  London Metal Exchange (LME)

©  201 4  SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company All rights reserved

Hedge / Hedging: a hedge is a position established in one market in an attempt to offset 
exposure to price fluctuations in some opposite position in another market with the goal of 
minimizing one's exposure to unwanted risk. There are many specific financial vehicles to 
accomplish this, including insurance policies, forward contracts, swaps, options, many types of 
over-the-counter and derivative products, and perhaps most popularly, futures contracts.
Public futures markets were established in the 1800s to allow transparent, standardized, and 
efficient hedging of agricultural commodity prices; they have since expanded to include futures 
contracts for hedging the values of energy, precious metals, foreign currency, and interest rate 
fluctuations. (Source: Wikipedia, http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hedge_(finance))
Companies not hedging their exposures arising from their day to day physical business (such 
as purchasing and/or selling commodities or products that contain commodities) are risking 
the profitability of their business due to unforeseeable price changes for commodities as 
commodities are typically and most often priced on market values (as shown in above copper 
price chart) and not fixed values. Price volatility of commodities increases e.g. arising from 
increased demand in China, but also as examples due to shortages or closures of mines, or 
due to weather or other events such as earthquakes, prices may change easily by + or -  5 % 
just within a day). Due to the increasing price volatility, it is of higher importance than ever 
before to hedge in order to stay profitable.
In the above example, the copper price is falling drastically (real data from LME London Metal 
Exchange for Copper). A metal converter company being exposed to the price risk on sales as 
well as on purchasing side is facing huge challenges in such a market situation, as the 
premium (processing fee) he earns is by far too low to make a gain or in this example even to 
cover the costs. In a well hedged scenario, the metal converter company focuses on the key 
strength to convert material at low costs, and be profitable through the processing fee, having 
managed the price volatility risk through hedging, in the example above purchasing & selling

Exchanges -  Key Characteristics

• Covered under Exchange Agreements - Standard contracts -  standard terms and conditions for all 
members of each Exchange

• Standard commodity lots (contracts) and products
• Uniform quantities -  per day or month
• Standard or single delivery location

Margining is daily - can be expensive in period of high volatility
• Requires buy and sell to eliminate physical delivery exposure 

Most futures and options never go to physical delivery
• Centralized execution is normal
• No or minimum credit exposure -  due to daily margining and loss sharing
• Can be transacted at portfolio level or transaction level

Highest liquidity of commodity financial instruments -  easy to access market -  customer can be 
invisible

Over the Counter (OTC) -  Key Characteristics

Covered under ISDA (international Securities Dealers Association) master contract -  standard 
contract for financial derivatives -  now includes physical energy -  allows for netting across multiple 
items for consolidated credit management -  important for banks due to buying and selling along with 
combination of physical and paper
Custom quantities -  important for manufacturers and smaller customers
Multiple locations -  concept of delivery location is same for paper and physical as the price is the 
index at the location for the delivery period

• No margining required -  combined with other financial instruments under ISDA and margin if 
exposure is great than the unsecured credit limit
Does not require two trades to complete hedge
Paper only -  no chance of physical delivery
Centralized execution is non standard -  regional expertise

• Credit exposure is counterparty dependent and unique 
Can be transacted at portfolio level or transaction level

• Liquidity dependent on market and term structure

OTC Commodity Instruments - Swap

• A commodity swap is an agreement whereby a floating (market, index or spot) price is exchanged 
for a fixed price over a specified period. A swap is identical to a sequence of forward contracts 
containing commitments to buy and sell an underlying commodity using different pricing 
mechanisms at different maturity dates.

Examples of the standard commodity swap
-  Party A  A  fixed price is paid to party B and a floating price is received from  Party B

-  Party A  A  floating price is paid to party B and a fixed price is received from Party B

• Another standard type of a commodity swap is a Basis swap where a floating price is paid for one 
commodity and a floating price is received for another commodity, with a differential representing the 
basis or locational price differences added to or subtracted from one side of the swap.
One of the advantages of swaps is that a market maker can tailor a swap to fit the needs of a 
particular counterparty, whereas standardization is the key to the success of exchange-traded 
instruments.
Commodity swaps are financially settled.

OTC Commodity Instruments - Options

A commodity option is a contract that allows the buyer of the option the right, but not the obligation, 
to buy or sell the commodity to the counterparty at a specified price and within a specified date 
range.
As compensation for this obligation, the seller of the option receives a premium.
European style options have a single exercise date, the expiration date of the option.
American style options can be exercised at any time during the option period.
When the option is in the money (when the market price has changed in the buyer’s favor), the 
owner (buyer) of the option will receive a cash payment from the seller for the difference of the 
option price and the market price at exercise date. If the option is out of the money nothing 
happens at expiration.
Most options are financially settled, a small percentage convert into physical purchases or sales.

OTC Commodity Instruments - Forwards

A commodity forward is an agreement whereby a physical sale or purchase is exchanged for a fixed 
or floating price for a specified period. A forward contract is an agreement between two parties to 
exchange at some fixed future date a given quantity of a commodity for a price defined today. The 
price today is known as the forward price.

Examples of the standard commodity forward
-  Party A  A  fixed price is paid to Party B for X X X  units o f Com m odity A  delivered in D ecem b er 201 4

One of the advantages of forwards is that a market maker can tailor a forward to fit the needs of a 
particular counterparty, whereas standardization is the key to the success of exchange-traded 
instruments.
Forwards are relatively unique in the metals and mining industries.
Commodity forwards can be physically or financially settled. An extremely low (less than 5%) 
percentage of forwards go to physical delivery. A specific action needs to be taken to prevent 
physical delivery (such as transacting the offset of the original transaction).

Exchange Traded Instruments - Futures

• A standardized contract for the purchase or sale of a commodity which is traded for delivery in the 
future.
Commodity futures are standardized in terms of the quantity, quality, and delivery time for each 
commodity-except the price which is determined (at the time the contract is entered into) according 
to the demand and supply situation. In practice, physical delivery of the commodity rarely occurs 
because future contracts are usually closed out before their expiration date.

• Traded on Exchanges as NYMEX, LME, CBOT,....
• Margin deposits are required to be provided to assure that potential losses are covered

-  Initial margins

-  Daily variation margins

Closing a future position is done by executing the reverse Future Contract, with a last margin 
posting (closing margin) calculated as the difference between last days closing price and the price 
paid for the closing contract.

Exchange Traded instruments -  Listed Options

• This instrument is the same financial instrument as the OTC option and has the same 
characteristics.
Listed Options on an exchange are standardized and provide a higher level of liquidity similar to a 
future.
Margin deposits are required to be provided to assure that potential losses are covered
-  Initial margins

-  Daily variation margins

Commodity Market Differences

M etal C om m o dities
Daily Futures at London Metal Exchange (LME)- Contracts for each day -  not monthly 
Monthly Futures at Chicago Mercantile Exchange

• Monthly average pricings for physicals & derivative transactions
Pricing for physicals frequently after delivery to counteract transportation risk 
(Typical example: Monthly average of month after commodity delivery)
No basis market 
For LME traded Metals

• No location differentials (warehouses all over the world)
• Limited OTC market for swaps

Hedging with Commodity Derivatives

Each company will have their own Hedging Strategy which is based on the amount of 
Commodity Risk the company is willing to take. This is covered in a Company’s Risk 
Policy.
In order to manage the commodity risk, financial derivatives (futures, options and swaps) 
are used.
There are two types of Commodity Risk
• Volume -  where the sales and purchase volumes do not equal

Price -  where the pricing structures of the respective purchase and sales contracts do not match 
(fixed vs. floating)

Hedging can be handled at two levels
• Specific transactions -  qualify for hedge accounting

Aggregated transactions (portfolio hedging) -  Does not qualify for hedge accounting

©  2 0 1 4  SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company All rights reserved Internal 27

0  Visit : www.erpexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

Hedging Strategy Logic

Sample Business Strategy 
• Use futures for long term hedging

For example - hedge 70% of forecast for years 2 to 5 out -  resulting in hedging of core commodity 
risk
Convert to swaps when delivery period gets closer, operations are defined
Swaps are used to manage price risk -  convert portfolios to price risk in compliance with company’s 
risk profile

Points of Consideration
Hedging is usually done at less than 100% of commodity needs to account for operational issues 
and normal fluctuation in production or consumption
Hedging can be consolidated into liquid commodities based on mathematical relationships 
-  Crude oil used as a proxy for propane

■  Talk Track:

From a business perspective Commodity Management consists of the these building 
blocks. On a very high level one can talk about 3 main areas: Commodity Trading (orange), 
Commodity Logistics (blue) and Commodity Risk Management (purple).

Almost all companies buying and/or selling commodities will have need for solutions for at 
least parts of the blue Commodity Logistics blocks and for Commodity Risk Management. 
The need for a Commodity Trading solution depends on the business model (i.e. is the 
company trying to also make money from trading commodities) and on the number of 
buying/selling transactions.

Market Data Based on DCS -  Definition

DCS is the ab brev ia tio n  fo r “ D erivative  C on trac t S p ec ific a tio n ’

R eflects  the real business w orld

B rings Logistics and Treasury c lo ser to gether

©  2 0 1 4  SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company All rights reserved

“DCS-Based Market Data” is the name given to the completely new data infrastructure that 
has been developed entirely from scratch in EhP7.

It is a powerful concept that, on the one hand, reflects the real business world and, on the 
other hand, brings Logistics and Treasury in Commodity Management closer together.

Regarding reflecting the business world: the entities that we have introduced are identical to 
the ones that can be found on an exchange, for example.

Already in previous releases, SAP offered integration between Logistics and Treasury. With 
the DCS-based infrastructure, we simplify that integration.

ISO 10383 defines the market identifier codes. As the market prices may be different for floor- 
traded futures and electronic traded futures, for example, market data has to be captured 
based on the market identified by the market identifier code.

Why Market Data Based on Derivative Contract Specification

A chieve a com m on understand ing  o f the traded  co m m od ity
Simplify communication between Logistics and Treasury

A chieve a com m on understand ing  o f an index
What is used for pricing?
What is the basis of a paper deal?

R educe the e ffo rt required to  cap tu re  m arket data fu tures issued da ily
• Data Feed 

Master Data Creation 
Commodity Curves

Use unified m arket data tab les  based on com m on entities

A llow  co m m od ity  curves to  be used in the C om m o d ity  Pricing Engine

©  2 0 1 4  SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved In te r n a l  8

Prior to EhP7, there was no uniform definition for traded commodities. To customize the 
integration of Logistics with Treasury, it was necessary to include application data 
(commodities) in Customizing for Logistics. It therefore became a goal of development to have 
a clear definition of commodities in Customizing.

Up until EhP6, there was no unique definition of an index. There was a need for a common 
understanding because the index is used in pricing and financial transactions are created on 
the basis of an index.

Especially in the metal industry, some exchanges issue daily futures, for example. When 
futures are issued with such a high frequency, this used to cause considerable manual effort 
for the creation of the required future master data (class data in SAP TRM) and the inclusion 
of these new futures in the market data feed and the commodity curves. One of the goals of 
development for EhP7 was to reduce the amount of effort involved.

Prior to EhP7, several market data tables existed in the system. One of the goals of the new 
development was to store the market data in unified market data tables.

An additional goal of development for EhP7 was to enable the commodity pricing engine 
(CPE) to use commodity curves for pricing.

Freight Tendering (RFQ) -  Table view
Fre ig h t R FQ  in form ation

The information o f the Freight R F Q  (with exception o f the stop and cargo information) is displayed in one 
row. It is not possible to expand a detail a rea  (like in the detail view). But it is the sam e information in detail 
and table view.
To perform an action for a freight R F Q  select one or more row and press the button in the top row 
To select more than one row hold control and click on each line or press the select all/deselect all button in 
the first row.
It is not possible to select m ore than row if you want to show the stop information or accept with changes

The DCS itself is just the definition of the attributes of a contract. A derivative that is traded for real can 
be identified by its DCS ID and a key date. The traded derivative has some characteristic periods such 
as a settlement period or a trading period that can also be captured.

■  In the block periods, the relevant periods for a key date can be either
Manually entered if no period determination method is defined on the Basic Data tab, or

■  Automatically derived according to the specified period determination method
In the case of automatic determination, the relevant logic is included in a BAdl implementation (see the 
section on Customizing).

■  The relevant periods for futures are:
• Contract Period

- Logical validity period of the future
• Cash Settlement Period

- Period in which cash settlement takes place
• Physical Settlement Period

- Period in which physical settlement takes place
• Trading Period

- Period in which the future is traded
• Quotation Period

- Period in which quotations are provided by the exchange
■  The relevant periods for listed options are:

• Contract Period
- Logical validity period of the listed option

• Trading Period
- Period in which the listed option is traded

• Quotation Period
- Period in which quotations are provided by the exchange 
Expiration Period
- Period in which the listed option expires

Functionality Overview

The C o m m o d ity  Pricing Engine is used to
• Calculate price components for products, which consist of commodities like metals, ore, oil or other 

commodities.
The price calculation is based on complex rules using real stock market and currency data. This 
should ensure that the price changes of the commodities are reflected in the products prices.

• Carry the complex rules, which are the result of business negotiations, throughout a whole business 
process (sales or purchasing or even link of both).

©  2 0 1 4  SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company All rights reserved Internal

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

@ SAP SE AC710 34

 Visit : www.erpexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

Functionality Overview - Coverage

The C o m m o d ity  Pricing Engine covers  com plex pricing rules
Define reference commodity (e.g. Arabic light crude oil or copper from London Metal Exchange)

• Averaging over time periods of quotations (e.g. last month)
Rules for dynamic period determination
Rules for currency conversion (e.g. daily or average)
Rules for quantity conversion

• Surcharge (e.g. your margin on top of the stock price)
• Rules for rounding steps
• High accuracy of intermediate calculation steps

(e.g. in oil industry n x 100 million US$ are sold / bought)
Analysis of intermediate calculation steps
Evaluation of complex rule (= formula) results in price and value

• Integration into net price calculation (like surcharges, taxes, etc.)

What is a CPE term? Definition

A C PE Term  is part o f a fo rm ula  and is ca lcu lated  in dep end en tly
• Results of different terms can be calculated, compared and selected (use the lowest, highest, etc.)

A formula can be split into parts with different time periods (to which stock market data and currency 
data correspond), different stock markets, different conversion rules (for currency and quantity) to 
allow a ‘mixed’ calculation

Its input data part can be
• predefined in customizing 

defaulted into CPE formulas in documents 
manually entered in CPE formulas in documents

©  2 0 1 4  SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company All rights reserved Internal

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

@ SAP SE AC710 72

 Visit : www.erpexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

What is a CPE term? Details

A C PE Term  in a do cu m en t consis ts  of:
Term number (continuous numbering in a formula)
Term key (link to customizing)

• Term Calculation type
• Numerator and denominator
• Absolute quantity and unit

Term Rule (link to Period Determination, Surcharge and Conversion Rules,...)
• Quotation Data (Source, Type, Number)
• Amount
• Currency 

Pricing quantity
• Pricing unit
• Reference document and item
• Provisional flag
• Term type

Reference to Conversion and Rounding 
Customer specific fields

• Status

Charge type for Rate Value (line-item  level)
You can say how much the rate value variance is acceptable to you. E.g. create a dispute 
tolerance with an upper limit amount of USD 1.50 for a line item with a rate amount of USD 5 for 
a charge type.

Charge type for Final am ount (line-item  level)
How much total value of the Charge type in the FO is acceptable to you. E.g. specify upper and 
lower limit amounts or percentages for a charge type for a final amount of a Charge item in a 
dispute case.

Total am ount of the FO (header level)
Example how much is the over all FO Total Charge amount variance is acceptable to you. E.g. 
specify upper and lower limit amounts or percentages for a total amount of a Freight Order in a 
dispute case.

Additional information:
Incase the entire dispute case is automatically approved by tolerance, the system by default 
does not approve the Dispute case. This is done to protect the carrier from getting instant results 
in such scenarios on the automatic approvals. To automatically close the dispute case, kindly 
use the Background report/SCMTMS/SET_CARRIER_RELEVANCE to close such dispute 
cases.

For Dispute Management the “Update Settl. Charges From Order” checkbox has to be 
mandatorily checked.
This flag (when checked) tells that whenever there is a change in FO/FB charges, on recalculate 
in settlement, these charges are copied to the settlement. If the charge type is explicitly changed 
in the settlement, then it becomes fixed in the settlement, in which case on recalculate in the 
settlement, the changes made to this charge type in the Freight Order does not flow into the 
settlement.

Note Tolerance and Workflow are both optional.
In order to enable the workflow, set the checkmark in the settlement profile of the carrier and 
assign the profile to the carrier (Vendor Org Data in the BP transaction) for the purchasing 
organization you have created approvers.

New Calculation Routines for Price Calculation -  Use

You can use the fo llow ing  new  ca lcu la tio n  routines in co m b ination  w ith a quotation  
group.

Calculation Routine 24 - Group Maximum per Date, then Average
Calculates the daily maximum of two or more quotation definitions 
and then averages across the quotation period.

Calculation Routine 25 - Group Minimum per Date, then Average
Calculates the daily minimum of two or more quotation definitions 
and then averages across the quotation period.

Calculation Routine 26 - Group Sum per Date, then Average
Calculates the daily sum of two or more quotation definitions 
and then averages across the quotation period.

Calculation Routine 26 - Group Sum per Date, then Average -
Example

You can use this calculation routine to calculate the daily difference of two price quotations, 
add a third price quotation and then average across the quotation period.
To do this you have to create a surcharge rule* (that multiplies the price quotation by -1) 
and assign it to the corresponding quotation group position.

Zero Price Quotation

©  2 0 1 4  SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved. In te r n a l  2 3

Zero Price Quotation -  Business Context

Price quotations can fluctuate  around zero.

When buying or selling a commodity, business partners might agree on a premium based 
on a basis differential.

For example buying or selling natural gas:
Henry Hub serves as the official delivery location for natural gas and sets the benchmark price for 
natural gas in the US.
The basis differential is the difference between the Henry Hub price quotation and the price of 
natural gas in another specified location (for example Chicago).
Therefore the price calculation of the premium based on the basis differential can lead to a zero 
price result that shouldn’t give an error at price calculation.

©  2 0 1 4  SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved. In te r n a l  24

@ SAP SE AC710 34

 Visit : www.erpexams.com

Multiple Provisional Terms - Business Context

W hen buying o r selling co m m od ities , you can agree w ith  yo u r business partner on a 
quotation  period from  w hich price qu otations are used fo r the ca lcu lation .

During deal capture, the quotation period can be completely in the future. For example, the 
month after the month of delivery.

Therefore, a provisional price calculation, that is based on a different quotation period, is 
sometimes required. This allows you to calculate a price prior to the end of the agreed final 
quotation period.

A provisional price calculation is needed at different points in time. For example:
To calculate a net value in the contract or order (for example credit limit check) during deal capture. 
To issue a provisional/differential invoice immediately after delivery.

©  2 0 1 4  SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved. In te r n a l  28

@ SAP SE AC710 88

 Visit : www.erpexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

Multiple Provisional Terms -  Use

P rovis ional price ca lcu lation

A different quotation period in a provisional term is used for provisional price calculation. 
A provisional term is assigned to either:
• a final term or
• another provisional term, that is, one can define chains of fall back terms 
Final price calculation

The agreed final quotation period in a final term is used for final price calculation.

For the price calculation, you can therefore have different quotation periods in the final 
invoice, in one or more provisional/differential invoices, and the contract/order itself.

Suppression of CPE Blocking Reason - Business Context

A final invoice m ust not be issued until a final price ca lcu la tion  can be executed .

When using price quotations for the calculation, the agreed final quotation period must be 
completely in the past.

Other price elements that influence the provisional price, but do not influence the invoice 
value (for example, used for controlling purpose), should not prevent a final invoice.

the final quotation period is not completely in the past and a provisional price is calculated.

The CPE Blocking Reason OP -  Provisional Price is assigned to a SD Billing Block in the 
CPE customizing.

• The SD Billing Block is assigned to the final invoice type in SD customizing.

business docum ent.

When changing the formula or term data in the business document, the following applies: 
• The formula or term key is removed.

The corresponding description can be changed and will be saved in the business document.

Integrate the CPE into Pricing
Create CPE Condition Types

©  2 0 1 4  SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company All rights reserved

■  The assignment of an access sequence is optional.

With this setting, you avoid that items with a non-CPE relevant material show the CPE 
condition type as incorrect in the business document.

■  Example:

There is a CPE condition type with an assigned access sequence containing the material as 
an access field.

• Material A: relevant for CPE

• Material B: not relevant for CPE

To have the CPE condition defaulted for material A in the business document you have to 
maintain a CPE condition record.

For material B you do not maintain a condition record for the CPE condition type. The CPE 
condition type is not defaulted for the item representing material B in the business document.

Otherwise, the CPE condition type would be displayed as incorrect in the business document.

Definition of Quotation Group

You can use quotation  groups fo r  ca lcu lating  a term  rate from  d ifferen t quotations.

This allows a price calculation for each day of the quotation period (for example, average 
per date).

A quotation group has the following characteristics:
Is defined in the CPE Customizing
SAP Customizing Implementation Guide /  Sales and Distribution /  Basic Functions /  Commodity 
Pricing /  Commodity Pricing Engine /  Definition of CPE Quotations / Define Quotation Group. *

Contains multiple quotation definitions
• Is assigned to a term

You can use a surcharge rule to  perform  fu rth er ca lcu la tio ns such as deductions or 
surcharges.

A Surcharge Rule has the following characteristics:

• Is created with either
• An absolute surcharge (for exam ple, 1 0 $ /T O ) or 

Factors (for exam ple, add 5% )

• Is defined in the CPE Customizing

■ Unit: Introduction to CPE

• ----
• ---- Lesson: Set up and use CPE Condition, CPE formula, and 
• --- CPE term

At the end of this exercise, you will be able to do the following:

• Set up CPE formula and CPE term

• Use CPE conditions in a business document

A mining company plans to use the CPE pricing in a business document, 
for example in a sales order. In addition to the classical pricing 
conditions, CPE conditions need to be set up, as well as CPE formula and 
CPE terms.

1 Create a sales order with a CPE condition

Customizing and Master Data Part

1-1-1 Check if copper price condition type CCOO is a CPE condition type.

1-1-2 Check pricing procedure CMCOP1. Are the settings for the CPE condition 
type CCOO correct?

1-1-3 Copy customer CM_CMT03 to your own customer ZZnn_CMT03 with nn > 
00 and fill all required fields.

1-1-4 Maintain the condition record for formula assembly for pricing condition type 
CCOO. Copy one of the entries with material CM_CU_CONC and replace the 
sold-to-party and ship-to-party with the customer you created in step 1-1-3.

Business Document Part

1-1-5 Create a sales order (type OR) with sold-to-party ZZnn_CMT03 and material 
CM_CU_CONC.

1-1-6 Open the sales order in change mode and navigate to the item conditions 
screen. Check which condition types are CPE relevant condition types.

condition type CCOO.

1-2-2 Enter a fixed rate of 500 USD/1 TCU and check, if the formula value changes.

1-2-3 Reset your changes with the Update button.

1-3 Use an existing CPE formula

If you prefer to use an already exiting formula and term, please use the following ones:
Formula T2_CU_FLT and term T2_CU_FLTF

1-3-1 Check in customizing, if term T2_CU_FLTF is assigned to formula 
T2_CU_FLT.

1-3-2 Check if formula assembly procedure 0CPEF1 exists and can be used for 
customer pricing procedure D.

1-3-3 Create a sales order (type OR) with customer CM_CMT03 and material 
TST2_CU_CONC.

1-3-4 Check if formula T2_CU_FLT is assigned to the copper price condition type.

1-4 Create a new CPE formula and use it in the sales order

1-4-1 To create a new formula with a new term, copy the available CPE term 
T2_CU_FLTF to a new one.

1-4-2 To use the new term in a new formula, copy CPE formula T2_CU_FLT to a 
new one. Save your settings. To this new CPE formula, assign the term you 
created in step 1.4.1. Delete the other terms.

1-4-3 Create a sales order (type OR) with sold-to-party CM_CMT03, ship-to-party 
CM20_CMT03 and material CM_CU_CONC. Enter your formula for 
condition type CCOO manually and check if the numbers of the terms have 
changed. Check if your term key is used in the formula.

1-4-4 In order to get the your new formula defaulted automatically in the sales order, 
you have to create a new condition record for formula assembly with the 
following values: Condition type OFOR, pricing condition type CCOO, sales 
organization 01, distribution channel 01, sold-to-party CM_CMT03, ship-to- 
party ZZnn_CMT03, material CM_CU_CONC, formula key of the formula 
you created before, today's date as valid-from date, and 31.12.9999 as valid-to 
date.

1-4-5 Create a sales order (type OR) with sold-to-party CM

1-4-6 _CMT03, ship-to-party ZZnn_CMT03 and material CM_CU_CONC.

1-4-7 Check if your new formula and term is now determined automatically for the 
copper price.

Unit: Introduction to CPE
Lesson: Set up and use CPE Condition, CPE formula, and 
CPE term

1-1 Create a Sales Order with CPE conditions

Customizing and Master Data Part

1-1-1 Navigate to SAP Customizing Implementation Guide/Sales and
Distribution/Basic Functions/Pricing/Pricing Control/Define Condition Types.

The calculation type Q is assigned to the condition type CCOO.

1-1-2 Navigate to SAP Customizing Implementation Guide/Sales and
Distribution/Basic Functions/Pricing/Pricing Control/Define and Assign 
Pricing Procedures.

In the dialog box, choose Maintain pricing procedures. Select pricing 
procedure CMCOP1 and go to the control data.

The requirement 425 is assigned to the CPE condition type CCOO.

1-1-3 Navigate to SAP Menu/Logistics/Sales and Distribution/Master Data/Business 
Partner/Customer/Create/Sales and Distribution or use transaction VD01 and 
create the customer with reference to customer CM20_CMT03.

1-1-4 Use transaction VCPE_MD and navigate to Maintain Condition for Formula 
Assembly. In the tree, select Pricing Cond. Type and choose the Select Records 
button. Enter the pricing condition type CCOO and click button ‘Execute'. 
Copy one of the entries with material CM_CU_CONC. Change the sold-to- 
party and the ship-to-party to the name of your customer created in step 1-1-3.

Business Document Part

1-1-5 Navigate to SAP Menu/Logistics/Sales and Distribution/Sales/Order/Create or 
use transaction VA01. Create a sales order (type OR) with the sold-to-party 
ZZnn_CMT03 and the material CM_CU_CONC.

1-1-6 Navigate to SAP Menu/Logistics/Sales and Distribution/Sales/Order/Change 
or use transaction VA02. Choose the button Item Condition Screen.

In the Pricing Elements: Tree view, select condition type CCOO and choose 
the Condition Details button. The calculation type Q is assigned to the 
condition.

Conditions button. Make a note of the Formula Value of condition type CCOO.

1 TCU and choose Enter. The formula value changes.

1-2-3 Choose the Update button and choose Pricing Type B in the subsequent dialog 
box.

1-3 Use an existing CPE formula

1-3-1 Navigate to SAP Customizing Implementation Guide/Sales and
Distribution/Basic Functions/Commodity Pricing/SD-Specific CPE 
Objects/Define CPE Formula. Go to Terms of Formula and select formula 
T2_CU_FLT. Term T2_CU_FLTF is assigned to formula T2_CU_FLT.

Distribution/Basic Functions/Commodity Pricing/CPE in SD Documents and 
check if the formula assembly procedure 0CPEF1 exists for an entry with 
customer pricing procedure (CuPP) D, division 01, distribution channel 01 and 
sales organization 01.

1-3-3 Navigate to SAP Menu/Logistics/Sales and Distribution/Sales/Order/Change 
or use transaction VA01 and enter all necessary data.

1-3-4 Go to the Item Conditions screen. On the Pricing Elements: Tree view, you
find the formula key T2_CU_FLT in the Condition Values section of condition 
type CCOO.

1-4 Create a new CPE formula and use it in the sales order

1-4-1 Navigate to SAP Customizing Implementation Guide /Sales and
Distribution/Basic Functions/Commodity Pricing/ Commodity Pricing 
Engine/SD-Specific CPE Objects/Define CPE Term. Choose the Copy as... 
button and enter a new name in the Term Key field. Save your settings.

1-4-2 Navigate to SAP Customizing Implementation Guide /Sales and
Distribution/Basic Functions /Commodity Pricing/ Commodity Pricing 
Engine/SD-specific CPE Objects/Define CPE Formula. Choose the Copy as... 
button and enter a new name in the Formula Key field. Save your settings. 
Navigate to the Terms of Formula, delete all terms and enter the term you 
created in step 1-4-1 in the Term Key field in the Terms of Formula sectioa 
Save your settings.

1-4-3 Navigate to SAP Menu/Logistics/Sales and Distribution/Sales Order/Create or 
use transaction VA01 and enter all necessary data. Go to the Item Conditions 
screen. On the Pricing Elements: Tree view, select condition type CCOO and 
enter your own formula key in the Formula Key field and choose ENTER. 
Select the term and go to the Term Values. The term key you created before is 
displayed.

1-4-4 Use transaction VCPE_MD and navigate to Maintain Condition for Formula 
Assembly. In the tree, select Pricing Cond. Type CCOO and choose the Select 
Records button.

Enter the following values: CCtC = OFOR, CTyp = CCOO, SOrg = 01, 
distribution channel = 01, division = 01, sold-to-party = CM20_CMT03, ship- 
to-party = ZZnn_CMT03, material = CM_CU_CONC, formula key = your 
formula, valid from = today's date, valid-to date = 31.12.9999.
Save your settings and leave the Customizing screen.

1-4-5 Navigate to SAP Menu/Logistics/Sales and Distribution/Sales/Order/Change 
or use transaction VA01 and enter the necessary data.

1-4-6 On the Pricing Elements: Tree view, your new formula and term is determined 
automatically for pricing condition type CCOO.

2nd Exercise: Work with multiple provisional terms

In the commodity business, the pricing period may be longer than the 
period between the contract negotiation and the final invoice. It may be 
necessary to use different provisional terms to allow provisional price 
determinations within different periods (for example, contract creation, 
deliveries, and final invoicing)

2-1 Define a CPE formula with three terms: one final term T1 and two provisional terms T2 
and T3. The period determination is similar to the figure above. Provisional term T3 is 
based on the available historical data when creating the document (for example, a 
contract). Provisional term T2 refers to provisional term T3 and has a period 
determination within the delivery horizon. The final term T1 refers to provisional term 
T2 and has a period determination within the agreed final quotation period. For 
example, average of the quotes of the month following the month after final delivery -  
1st MAMA (month after month of arrival).

2-1-1 Check the available period determination rules and create new ones if 
necessary for the following:

• provisional term (fall back): for example, the previous month

• provisional term: month of arrival
• final term: month after month of arrival

2-1-2 Check the available CPE terms and create new ones if necessary

2-1-3 Create a new CPE formula that includes the three terms and the correct 
relationships between the provisional terms and the final term

3rd Exercise: Use the concept of blocking reason suppression

CPE includes an option to set billing blocks automatically. This is used if 
a final price cannot be determined because the agreed quotation period 
end is in the future. In this case, a final invoice must not be issued. 
However, there may be situations where the blocking reason should not 
be set, for example, when CPE conditions are only set up as statistical 
conditions. A new setup allows the suppression of the blocking reason 
setting for specific applications, depending on the condition type.

3-1 Check the available application specific blocking reason settings for Sales and 
Distribution in the system, and create a new entry if necessary

3-1-1 Note the condition types that are available

3-1-2 Set up blocking reason suppression for a condition type used in an SD pricing 
scheme, with CPE-relevant conditions

3-2 Create a business document (for example, a sales order), and check if the blocking 
reason is set or not.

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

@ SAP SE AC710 143

 Visit : www.erpexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

4th Exercise: Use zero price within a CPE calculation

Bonus and penalty conditions in commodity management business are 
often calculated as an adjustment against the base price For example, the 
adjustment = difference between two commodity quotations published on 
different locations like Crude Oil listing “WTT and “Brent”.

This difference could lead to a zero adjustment in the price -  which in 
SAP ERP pricing would lead to error messages, because conditions with 
zero price result are not allowed. But to enable such calculations, 
conditions with zero price now are accepted.

4-1 Construct a situation where CPE condition result is zero

4-1-1 Option 1: Use two terms that use different quotations (for example LME and 
NYMEX Quotes), where the quotes at a specific date, or the average quotes 
over a specific period are equal.

4-1-2 Option 2: Use one quotation where the maintained quote is zero on a specific 
date.

4-1-3 Option 3: Use two terms with identical quotations and the calculation rule is 
SUM o f Terms. Adjust one term by a factor of -1.

4-1-4 Option 4: Use two CPE-based conditions where the term result values are
identical on a specific date or for a specific period. Use a 3rd condition where 
the value is the result of reference conditions (CPE formula or CPF formula)

4-2 Create a business document (for example, a sales order), where the CPE term result is 
zero according to 4-1

4-2-1 Check that the zero value in pricing is accepted without displaying an error 
message.

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

@ SAP SE AC710 144

 Visit : www.erpexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

5th Exercise: Manipulate the term key description in a business 
document

If the user manipulates a CPE formula or term in a business document, 
the description for formula or term (that are retrieved from Customizing) 
are removed. The user now has the option to adjust the descriptions of 
formula and term.

5-1 Create a sales order and adjust a term setting, for example, the surcharge rule of the 
provisional term

5-1-1 Check that the term key is removed.

5-1-2 Change the term’s description (for example, Prov. Term + surcharge)

5-1-3 Save the document.

5-2 Check that the description has been saved with the document data

5-2-1 Display the created document and check if the new term description is 
available

1-3-1 Replace the term (or the entire formula) for the appropriate condition, with the 
term that calculates the daily maximum of the two quotation definitions and 
then averages across the quotation period.

The formula assigned to the copper price condition (here CC00) is replaced by 
the formula key.

As expected, the formula value 7859,92 USD/Tonnes copper is the average of 
the daily maximum of the two quotation definitions.

of the daily maximum of the two quotation definitions is the term value.

2-1 Define a CPE formula with three terms: one final term T 1 and two provisional terms T2 
and T3. The period determination is similar to the figure above. Provisional term T3 is 
based on the available historical data when creating the document (for example, a 
contract). Provisional term T2 refers to provisional term T3 and has a period 
determination within the delivery horizon. The final term T 1 refers to provisional term 
T2 and has a period determination within the agreed final quotation period. For 
example, average of the quotes of the month following the month after final delivery -  
1st MAMA (month after month of arrival).

2-1-1 Check the available period determination rules and create new ones if 
necessary

The Answer: Configurable Parameters and Formulas (CPF)

C PF Form ula (Example)
A C P F fo rm ula  consists  o f free ly  
definab le  param eters  and fu nction s  Formula parameters
fo r a ca lcu lation .

ActmlMoisture.AgreedMoisture.BasePenaUy,Increment

The system  stores  the param eter  
values to g e th er w ith the business  
docum ent, and carries  them  Function of SAP Business Rule Framework 

th ro u g h o u t the w ho le  business  plus (BRFplus)

process. n , A c tu a lMoisture A g re ed MoiSture
P e n a lty  = ----------------------------------------* BasePp„„,tv

In c re m en t
A fte r you assign a C P F fo rm ula to  a

Define Entries for Parameter Catalog

■  Definition CPF Elementary Data Type:

Data type of fixed or variable length that is neither structured nor a table type or reference 
type. There are the following CPF elementary data types:

-  CPF value: Consists of a number and a currency field.

CPF price rate: Consists of a number, a currency, a price unit, and a unit of measure 
field.

-  CPF quantity: Consists of a number and a unit of measure field.

Overlap means the resource was planned multiple times and is therefore not executable. An 
example is, if the trailer is already planned and newly planned in a next step. This would cause 
an overlap which the user gets displayed as a red line.

Similar to the utilization view an overlap view shows if several documents on a resource overlap. 
This overlap can be overcome by scheduling the resource.

Benefits of CPF

• Use the CPF to calculate the condition base, condition rate, and condition value.

You can freely define the parameters for a CPF formula. The parameter values are stored 
together with the business document and carried throughout the whole process.

• Parameter values can be retrieved automatically in the business document from various data 
sources (for example, from a batch). Alternatively, you can manually enter a parameter value.

CPF formulas and parameter values can be defaulted in the business document.

For a parameter, you can define a scale to determine the value of the parameter.

Penalty with Scale

Im agine, the penalty  exam ple  looks a bit d ifferent:

If the actual moisture content o f the commodity exceeds
the agreed moisture content, the value will be reduced
by a certain amount in USD/TO for each 0.1% over the agreed moisture content.

The penalty depends on the actual moisture content:

Moisture Content in % Base Penalty in USD/TO

5 to 7 0 .50

7 to 8 0 .75

8 to 9 1.00

9 to 30 1.10

Data Source
Parameter Catalog and Custom Structure

• Create a new parameter in the parameter catalog.
Assign data type SAP_QUALITY, which is predefined by SAP and contains 2 components: the name 
of the characteristic and the value.

• The data source routine allows a parameter value to be derived from a source other than the Ul or 
condition master record.

Parameter Mapping
Use Case

Penalties other than for moisture (for example, arsenic, bismuth, and so on) can be 
calculated using the same BRFplus formula.
In this case, it is better to use generic names for the parameters of the BRFplus function, 
like actual quality and agreed quality (instead of actual moisture or agreed moisture).

This increases the reusability of a BRFplus function.
However the parameters of the BRFplus function and the parameters of the CPF formula 
do not match anymore.

BRFplus function with generic nam es

Cumulative Graduated Scales
Use Case

For example, a certain surcharge or discount has 3 parameters: Market Price, Base Price, and 
Percentage Discount.

The surcharge is calculated as follows: Base Price * Percentage Discount 

The Base Price is represented as a scale, using the Market Price as a base.

Market Price in USD/TO Base Price Level in USD/TO

4 0 0 0  to 800 0 0 ,06

800 0  to 900 0 0 ,04

900 0  to 10000 0

10000  to 12000 -0 ,0 3

12000  to 5 0000 -0,01

As the market price is expected to be between 9000 and 10000, there is no surcharge or discount 
within this range.

©  2 0 1 4  SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company All rights reserved Internal

If base value and scale level have different currencies and/or units of measure, conversions 
will take place automatically.

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

@ SAP SE AC710 214

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

Cumulative Graduated Scales
Start of Ascending Scale and Start of Descending Scale

If the market price is below 9000 USD/TO, a calculation will take place for each scale line, from the 
market price up to 9000.
If the market price is above 10000 USD/TO, a calculation will take place for each scale line, from 
the market price down to 10000.
This results in 2 scales emerging. One ranges from 9000, down to 4000, and the other ranges from 
10000 and up to 50000.

Market Price in Base Price Level in Market Price in Base Price Level in 
USD/TO USD/TO USD/TO USD/TO

4 0 0 0  to 800 0 0,06 4 0 0 0  to 8000 0,06

800 0  to 900 0 0,04 800 0  to 900 0 0,04

900 0  to 10000 0 Market Price in Base Price Level in 
USD/TO USD/TO

1 0000  to 12000 -0 ,0 3
10000  to 12000 -0 ,0 3

1 2000  to 5 00 00 -0,01
12000  to 50000 -0,01

For this reason, 9000 is called the S tart o f  D escend ing  Scale  and 10000 is called the S tart o f 
A scend ing  Scale.

at the next Scale Level. current Scale Level.

1-5 Determine a parameter value using a scale

the value of parameter Base_Penalty is to be determined as follows:

Actual Moisture Content (Actual_Moisture) Base_Penalty

Is greater or equal than 5% and lower than 7% 0.50 USD/TO

Is greater or equal than 7% and lower than 8% 0.75 USD/TO

Is greater or equal than 8% 1.00 USD/TO

the value of parameter Base_Penalty is to be determined as follows:

Actual Moisture Content (Actual_Moisture) Base_Penalty

Is greater or equal than 5% and lower than 7% 0.50 USD/TO

Is greater or equal than 7% and lower than 8% 0.75 USD/TO

Is greater or equal than 8% 1.00 USD/TO

Business Context

Pricing w ith Q uota tions o f C o m m o d ity  D erivatives

Price agreements may refer to quotations of commodity derivatives over a contractual 
period of time -  the quotation period (QP).

Valuation  o f Q uotation  Period in A dvance

Long before a QP begins, its QP entries need to be valuated, for example for the following 
use cases:

• Orders (for example, contract, sales order, purchase order)

• Period End Valuation (PEV)

• Invoice Forecast

• Credit Check

No historic prices as with an alternative QP are desired nor a substitution of the missing 
quotations by the current quotation. Instead, the current prices of derivatives should be 
used to valuate a QP entry.

Valuation of Quotation Period in Advance

Use C o m m o d ity  C urve fo r Q P en tries  in the fu ture

Use a commodity curve to valuate the QP entries that are still in the future. The result is 
used as current quotation forecast.

Typically required for internal purposes only, as period-end valuation or invoice forecast 
and not part of a contractual agreement with a business partner.

Benefits

Q u ota tion s o f C om m o dity  D erivatives can be eas ily  accessed:

Simple reference to derivatives relative to the current quotation date using the Time to 
M atu rity  option.

Separate identification of the trading platform as Market Identifier Code (MIC).
• Unifies spot price quotations and quotations of commodity futures.

• From a quotation its derivative can be easily identified by its DCS and ke y  date (for 
example, its settlement or last trading date).

C om m o d ity  C urve eas ily  va luates Q P  entries in advance

• Only a commodity curve type is required to determine the curve.

• Invoices and credit memos can easily be excluded.

Derivatives no longer need to be maintained manually for a DCS-based commodity 
curve.

Exercise

9 ■ Unit: Quotation Forecast
• ---
• --- Lesson: Set up and use DCS-Based Quotations and 
• --- Quotation Forecast

At the end of this exercise, you will be able to do the following:

• Use DCS-based quotations

• Use Quotation forecast

• Verify the DCS-based quotations and quotation forecast results

A company sells copper cathode. They agreed on an average price with a 
contractual partner, based on the copper cash price at the London Metal 
Exchange (LME). At the time of sales order creation, some of the 
quotation period (QP) is in the future.

However, a price should be forecast for the entries in the quotation period 
that have quotation dates in the future by using a Derivative Contract 
Specification (DCS)-based commodity curve.

The same settings are valid for mark-to-market, but the price should no 
longer change after the goods issue date.

Note: You should do the exercise Capturing DCS-Based Market Data in advance. Use the 
quotation definition for which you already created the price quotations.

If no price quotations are retrieved in step 1-3.2.2.4, the DCS-based market data are not yet 
available. In this case, for the quotation definition you use in the term, execute report 
ZTBA_PRICEQUOT_RANDOM with the following data:

Key date from: Today’s date

Keydate to: End of this year (Caution: Do not use the default date) 

Price Date From: Start date of your quotation period 

Price Date To: Today’s date

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

@ SAP SE AC710 251

 Visit : www.erpexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

1-1 Create a term in CPE Customizing with a quotation definition based on DCS.

Copy the existing term T2_CU_FLTF and change the quotation definition to a DCS- 
based quotation using the cash price for copper at the LME. Use the following DCS- 
based quotation definition (## is the number of your group):

• DCS ID: T2CU##

• MIC: XLME London Metal Exchange

• Price type: ##+10

• Time to maturity: CASH

Maintain a quotation forecast routine to allow forecast values for the quotation period 
dates in the future.
Commodity Curve Type 3 —Commodity Curve Contract Style should be used for the 
quotation forecast.

Save the term.

1-2 Create a formula in the CPE Customizing and assign the term created in step 1-1.

Copy the existing formula T2_CU_FLT. Go to the assigned terms of the formula, delete 
the existing entries, and choose Save. Then add the term that you created in step 1-1 to 
the formula.

Save the formula.

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

@ SAP SE AC710 252

 Visit : www.erpexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

1-3 Create a sales order

1-3.1 Create a sales order using the following details: order type: OR, sales
organization: 0001, distribution channel 01, sold-to-party: CM20_CMT03, 
material: TST2_CU_CAT, quantity: 100 TO.

1-3.2 Go to the sales order item Conditions tab and choose the Pricing Elements: 
Tree view.

Adjust the price elements according to the price agreement as mentioned in the 
following steps. Afterwards, verify the retrieved price quotations and the 
quotation forecast result.

1-3.2.1 Select condition type CCOO - Copper Price.

1-3.2.1.1 To calculate the copper price, delete the default formula 
key (Condition Values area) and assign the formula that 
you created in step 1-2. The term you assigned to the 
formula is displayed in the Pricing Elements: Tree view.

1-3.2.2 Adjust the CPE term and verify the evaluation result.

1-3.2.2.1 Ensure that the Read Until Routine is set to 2 “Read into 
Future ” in the term setting. The entries of the quotation 
period that have quotation dates in the future will be 
considered and quotation forecast is possible.

1-3.2.2.2 Maintain the quotation period that it is partly in the future.

1-3.2.2.3 Check the date of the used evaluation key date.

1-3.2.2.4 Verify the retrieved price quotations.
Compare the price quotations for the quotation dates in the 
past with the entries in the DCS-based market data.

1-3.2.2.5 Verify the quotation forecast result and find the forecast 
values in the DCS-based commodity curve.

1-3.2.2.5.1 Which commodity ID and commodity curve 
type do you need to enter in the commodity 
curve master (transaction TANCCMASTER)?

considered and quotation forecast is possible.

CCOO.

Price condition does not change after the goods issue date.

1-4.2 Post a goods issue.

Market Price.

• Verify the quotation forecast result and find the forecast values in the DCS- 
based commodity curve.

» Check which curve reading date is used.

The curve reading date is the date from when the forecast value was taken. 
As the last trading date is used by the expiration date logic of the DCS, the 
curve reading date is the last trading date. The time to maturity is a relative 
time offset that identifies the derivative on the current quotation date (for 
example, 3 months).

A forecast value is requested for the 3 months future copper price on the 
18th of July. The curve reading date is the 16th of October. This is the last 
trading date for a derivative with the key date 18th of October.

Motivation: Pricing with Commodity Futures

Issue: C apturing  quotations fo r co m m o d ity  fu tures
A better support for quotations of commodity futures is required: A commodity future is a 
standardized contract to purchase or sell a commodity on or before a future date.

The future date for financial or physical 
An exchange defines a contract settlement is a key date that identifies a 
specification for trading commodity 

single commodity future of such a contract 
futures.

specification.

Generally speaking, a com m od ity  deriva tive  is identified by its contract specification and 
key date. Spot price quotations and quotations of commodity futures are just examples 
of that.
Several trading platforms may exist for a single contract specification.

Add contract specification, key date and trading 
platform to new market data model.

Pricing with Derivative Contract Specifications

B enefit: S im p lifies  the handling o f co m m o d ity  m arket data

A deriva tive  co n tra c t spec ifica tion  (DCS) contains the rules and conditions that are agreed 
upon at an exchange, and form the contract basis for trading with a specific commodity, or 
for a specific financial instrument

Each quotation has a ke y  da te  that identifies the derivative of a DCS.

The tim e to m a tu rity  (for example, 3 months) is a relative time offset that identifies the 
derivative on a current quotation date.The actual key date does not have to be known in 
this case.

• The trading platform can be specified explicitly by a m arke t id en tifie r code.

Market identifier code Trading platform

Price type Opening, closing, settlem ent and so on

quotation date + time to maturity* 3  M onths  on 2 0 .0 6 .2 0 1 3

Motivation: Quotation Forecast

Issue: Valuation  o f fu ture  quotation  period
• The price is based on quotations during a given period of time, the quotation period (QP).
• The QP is not fully in the past, thus the final price cannot be determined.
• The QP entries need to be valuated long before the quotation period begins.

Quotations Quotations not yet available

Example Use Cases for Quotation Forecast

• Period-End Valuation (PEV)
For PEV, you typically cannot wait until all QPs are in the past. Instead, you need the net 
price calculated with the best known values for the price quotations at the requested 
evaluation key date.

• Invoice Forecast
You need to simulate a final invoice that will be created in the future but not all quotations 
are available yet.

• Credit Check
A credit check needs to be passed before a shipment can be loaded. At this point in time, 
the agreed QP is typically not fully in the past.

Quotation Forecast with Commodity Curve

M otivation
• A commodity curve uses the currently traded prices of commodity futures or other 

derivatives and therefore reflects the current market prices for future settlements.
A commodity curve already incorporates the market price expectation for the future 
settlements.

• Quotations of commodity derivatives are available that will be settled at a time close to 
when the pending QP entries will be settled.
Interpolation between available quotations can be used to get a value for each QP entry 
that is still not quoted.______________________________________________

Use commodity curve with current market prices

Quotation Forecast with DCS-based Commodity Curve

Q uotation  Forecast

Quotation forecast provides an instant valuation of future QP entries. It uses the current 
prices of a DCS-based commodity curve from Treasury and  R isk  M anagem en t (TRM).

B enefits

• No fallback QP of a provisional term is required for this purpose anymore. However, 
it can still be used for a provisional invoice.

Just a commodity curve type is required when using DCS-based quotations.

You can easily prevent quotation forecast values from being used in invoices.

Derivatives used by the commodity curve no longer need to be maintained manually 
because the DCS has a period determination logic that enables the identification of 
relevant derivatives at runtime.

On 18.06., the copper future with key date 18.09. can also be referenced as a time to maturity 
of 3 months.

■  On 17.06., the same copper future can only be referenced by its key date.

On 17.06., the 3 months futures price is the price of the copper future with key date 17.09.

On 18.06., the copper spot price is the one of the copper future with key date 20.06.

■  Spot prices are a subset of futures’ prices:

• Time to maturity is zero, could be named Cash.

• Spot prices use a special price type (for example, Spot).

Note: The shown quotations are random numbers only. Typically, real world quotations in 
USD will not have 6 decimals.

What is a Commodity Curve?

C o m m o d ity  curve uses curren t prices

A commodity curve uses the current prices of commodity derivatives that have a financial 
or physical settlement in the future (for example, commodity futures).

Price on 2 6 .0 6 . for C o m m od ity  c u rv e  on
derivative that expires 
on 21 .08 .

Interpolated price on 
2 6 .0 6 . for expiration 
on 01 .08 .

As derivatives are available for only some dates in the future, the curve needs to 
interpolate between the available derivatives’ quotations.

From Market Data to Commodity Curves

Prices of Copper Futures

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company All rights i

There are two time dimensions for the quotations of a commodity derivative:

• The fix key date of the derivative

• The current quotation date.

Commodity Curve Uses Fix Quotation Date*

Prices for Curve Date 4.7.
(fix D C S , M IC , price type, quotation  d ate  =  curve  date )

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company All rights reserved Internal 22

A commodity curve uses a fix quotation date (also called price date) for all key dates.

More precise, the commodity curve tries using the same quotation date for all quotations but it 
may also use older quotations if necessary and allowed by the read back procedure of the 
commodity curve master.

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

@ SAP SE AC710 294

Commodity Curve Adds Interpolation

Commodity Curve
(fix  D C S , M IC , price type, quotation  d ate  =  cu rve  date )  
d efined  by cu rve  type  in com m odity  c u rv e  m aster

USD/ TO

Expiration Date:

When constructing a commodity curve, 
its grid points are not directly placed 
over their key dates.

The DCS-specific expiration date logic 
places them on the x-axis. For 
example, over their last trading date.

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company All rights reserved

■  A commodity curve contains the following:

• A fix quotation date (curve date) for which quotations are requested.

• The expiration date of a (potential) derivative which is currently asked for.

Quotation forecast first maps a pending QP entry to where it will expire on the x-axis of the 
commodity curve (for example using the last trading date) and reads the curve value at this x- 
axis position.

The used evaluation key date -  which is introduced later in this presentation -  is used as 
curve date.

Need to Replace the Quotation UoM for CPE?

Issue: Pricing of the contained commodity content only
If only the contained commodity content of a sales or purchase order item needs to be priced, its 
content is typically expressed as a conversion factor between different unit of measures (UoMs).
For this purpose, a special UoM must be defined in Logistics (for example, TCU for tons of pure 
copper). Pricing in CPE will then be based on this specific UoM.
Although the quotation UoM (for example TO) now differs literally from the logistics UoM (for example 
TCU), they are still semantically identical (1 TCU = 1000 KG = 1 TO).

Sales order item 100 TO copper concentrate 

Copper content 33% pure copper content 

as UoM conversion 3 TO = 1 TCU
(TCU = tons of pure copper) 

Copper quotations USD/ TO

Priced quantity 33 TCU

How does CPE know that the quotation UoM TO is identical to TCU?

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company All rights reserved Internal 26

Quotation Forecast in Invoices and Credit Memos?

Enable/ disable quotation forecast per current business process
A Forecast Mode is automatically set for the current business process. It indicates whether a quotation 
forecast is expected or not.
The forecast mode is set in the following cases:

Period-end valuation (PEV)
• Any CPE document category except invoices and credit memos 

Forecast routine
Checks the forecast mode and provides forecast values. Two implementations are delivered:

1) Read Curve if Document Permits
R e tu rn s  fo recas t v a lu e s  only if th e  fo recas t m ode is set.

2) Always Read Curve
R e tu rn s  fo recas t v a lu e s  in d epen den tly  from  fo rec a s t m ode.

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company All rights reserved Internal 33

■  Forecast mode:

For CPE document categories in the form of an invoice, the forecast mode is not set by 
default. This is because forecast values are typically for internal purposes only rather than 
as part of contract negotiations.

The automatic determination of the forecast mode can be overridden by providing KOMK- 
FORECAST_MODE (for example, in a user exit during pricing or in the Customizing 
activity Filter and Map Document Data).

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

@ SAP SE AC710 305

A DCS-based commodity curve can be derived from the DCS ID, MIC, and commodity curve 
type. If you are using DCS-based quotations, the DCS ID and MIC are defaulted from your 
quotation definition. In this case, all that is required for the determination of the commodity 
curve, is the commodity curve type.

However, you could also choose an alternative DCS ID and an alternative MIC. If, for 
example, no future contracts are available for your DCS ID -  which could be used to build a 
commodity curve -  you could enter an alternative DCS ID and MIC which are then used for 
the forecast values only.

How to find the forecast values in the commodity curve?

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company All rights reserved Internal

The used evaluation key date (see following slides) is 20.06.2013 (not shown).

■  As the QP has entries beyond the 20.06.2013, the forecast routine is called.

Forecast routine 1 Read Curve If Document Permits checks the forecast mode that is set in 
our case (not shown).

The commodity curve for DCS ID T 2 C U ,  MIC XLME, curve type 202, and the used 
evaluation key date (20.06.2013) as curve date are requested.

A commodity curve master was found for the commodity ID TST2_COPPER_LME and curve 
type 202. You can use the commodity ID for navigating to the curve master data using 
transaction TANCCMASTER, or to the curve directly using transaction TPM_TRCO_DCSMD.

The quotation for the used evaluation key date (20.06.2013) already exists (green status icon) 
so there is no need for a forecast value anymore. Typically, however, the used evaluation key 
date is the current date for which no quotations are yet available. In this case, a forecast value 
would have been requested also for current date as well.

A forecast value is displayed with a yellow status icon (a warning) which indicates that the 
current value is not the final one.

All forecast values also have a curve date and curve reading date. The curve date is the 
actual curve date that was used and may differ from the used evaluation fey date in case of 
read backs.

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

@ SAP SE AC710 308

 Visit : www.erpexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

The curve reading date is the date from when the curve value was actually taken. Let’s look at 
two examples:

1. The 1sf forecast value in the given example is requested for the 3 months future copper 
price on 21.06.2013. In our case this is a derivative with the key date 20.09.2013. Our 
commodity curve positions quotations over the last trading date, that is, we would find the 
key date 20.09.2013 over the last trading date which is in our case the 18.09.2013. This is 
why the curve reading date for the 3 months price on 21.06. is the 18.09.2013. In this case, 
we also hit a grid point of the curve with the key date 20.09.2013. We can take its quotation 
as forecast value for the price on 21.06. (the forecast value for 21.06. is actually the 
quotation from 20.06.2013).

2. The 2nd forecast value is for the 3 months future copper price on 24.06.2013. Its derivative 
will have a key date of 24.09.2013. Its last trading date is 2 days previous, that is, the 
22.09.2013, but due to the weekend, it is shifted to Friday, 20.09.2013. This is why the 
curve value is taken from the 20.09.2013. In this case, no grid point of the curve is hit and 
we need to interpolate between the adjacent ones. Due to the constant interpolation of our 
curve, we take the value of the previous grid point that is the same as in the 1st example.

■  Curve Date and Price Dates of contract data (blue frames):

The curve date displayed by the CPE in the list of used quotations needs to be entered to 
display the commodity curve in transaction TPM_TRCO_DCSMD. The actual price date (see 
Contract Data tab) of the grid points matches the curve date if no Read Back occurred.

■  Reading Date and End of Period date of contract data (gold frames):

■  CPE displays the curve reading date (column Read. Date). In transaction 
TPM_TRCO_DCSMD, on the Graphical Display tab, enter the 1st and last curve reading date 
as the start and end dates. The dates for which quotations were found are highlighted. The 
Contract Data tab lists all of the quotations. You can find the curve reading dates in the End of 
Period column. The period that is shown here, with Start of Period and End of Period, is 
determined by the expiration date logic of the DCS.

Used Evaluation Key Date

Evaluation of non-final QP depends on date and time
Unless the QP is in the past, the calculated price will change with each upload of missing 
quotations. In this time period, the formula evaluation also depends on its date (and time): 
the Used Evaluation Key Date.

The used evaluation key date

reflects how up-to-date the price is.

• is either today’s date (default) or a date in the past.

• is used as the curve date in a quotation forecast.

Latest Evaluation Key Date

Reference date as latest evaluation key date
For some use cases (for example, mark-to-market) the price should no longer change 
after a certain event.

For example, if the price should no longer change after the goods issue, all subsequent
price evaluations must lead to the same result as on the day of the goods issue posting.

For these use cases, the used evaluation key date can be limited by a reference date 
used as Latest Evaluation Key Date.

Requested Evaluation Key Date

Transactions can request an evaluation key date
By default, the price evaluation is requested for the current system date and time.

However, a period-end valuation, for example, may request the price as if it was 
calculated using a day in the past while an invoice forecast, on the other hand, can 
request the price evaluation for a future date.

For this purpose, the transaction can Formula Settings
Combination Routine 1 Lowest Term v

override the Requested Evaluation Key Splitting Routine 1 Whole Quantity for every Term v

Date.
Latest Eval. Keydate 50 Frst Goods Issue Posting Date v

I Req. Eval. Key Date 20.06.2013 16:16:51
However, the used evaluation key date is 
never beyond the latest evaluation key date F orm ula  settings in tre e  detail v ie w  o f th e  n ew  pricing Ul

or the current system date.

Requested Evaluation Key Date, 
Used Evaluation Key Date =  M in{ Latest Evaluation Key Date, }

System Date

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company All rights reserved

The transaction may also request an evaluation key date in the future. Although the used 
evaluation key date is still the current system date or the latest evaluation key date, the 
formula is evaluated as if the results were retrieved on the requested evaluation key date. 
Thus, a requested evaluation key date in the future has an impact on the formula status.

The used evaluation key date cannot be a date in the future. Thus, a quotation forecast will 
never try using a commodity curve with a future curve date.

Impacts of the Read Until Routine

Definition
The Read Until Routine defines the date up to when QP entries are used. QP entries 
beyond this date are ignored.

Use
Quotation forecast considers the part of the QP that is in the future -  seen from the used 
evaluation key date. If the read until routine returns a date on or before the used 
evaluation key date, no quotation forecast occurs. The read until routine, therefore, has 
the following impacts on quotation forecast:

• Read until routine 1 Read Until Now  is used if only the QP entries up to the 
requested evaluation key date need to be considered. In an invoice forecast, for 
example, this could be a date in the future. Otherwise, it is the system date or a date 
in the past and no quotation forecast is possible.

• Read until routine 2 Read Into Future is used if all QP entries need to be considered 
as it is required for quotation forecast.

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company All rights reserved Internal 44

No quotation forecast is possible after the read until date. For this reason, you should 
choose the read until routine 2 “Read Into Future” unless you need to restrict a quotation 
forecast to simulation purposes only.

Example 1

Two Forwarding Orders are assigned to a Freight Order. 

Aggregate (Complete) is selected as Strategy in the TCCS.

Example 2

Two Forwarding Orders are assigned to a Freight Order.

Copy Active (Selective) is selected as Strategy in the TCCS.

Example 3
Two Forwarding Orders are assigned to a Freight Order.
Copy Inactive (Complete) is selected as Strategy in the TCCS.

Note: no matter if one or many Forwarding Orders are assigned to the Freight Order, the cost pull 
calculation is only possible AFTER distributing the costs from the Freight Order to the Forwarding 
Order(s).
Exception: The Copy Inactive Strategy requires a 1:1 relationship between Forwarding Order and 
Freight Booking -  it is only relevant for an IATA direct scenario.

For Air Scenario:
The AWB charges are pulled if the COPY INACTIVE is maintained as cost pull strategy.
The Settlement charges are pulled if the COPY ACTIVE is maintained as cost pull strategy.

Business Context: Purpose of Price Fixation Options

The sales and purchase of commodities are based on complex calculation rules.
Price negotiations between a buyer and seller can result in the following:
• A floating1price (market price on future dates)
• A fixed price
• A mixture of a floating and a fixed price

Typically, a floating price is defined as a starting price for the whole pricing-relevant 
quantity. A price fixation option allows you to replace the floating price either for parts or for 
the whole pricing-relevant quantity with an agreed fixed price.

Price risks for a floating price, a fixed price and a price fixation option are considered 
differently as the existence of a price fixation option might require a different form of 
hedging.

'V a rio u s  d ifferent e xp ress io n s  a re  u sed  in com m odity  bus iness , e .g . unpriced, price to be fixed, non-fixed

© 2014 S A P  S E  o r  a n  S A P  affilia te  c o m p a n y . All r ig h ts  r e s e r v e d .  Internal 2

Usage of Price Fixation Options
