Contract with Price Fixation 
Option

©  2 0 1 4  S A P  S E  o r  a n  S A P  affilia te  c o m p a n y  All r ig h ts  r e s e r v e d Internal

A price fixation option allows the business partners to replace a floating price with an agreed 
fixed price for parts or for the whole scheduled quantity. The price fixation option consists of 
two parts: the definition and the exercises.

The definition of the price fixation option allows users to capture contractual details such as 
the following:

An exercise period or a latest exercise date up to which the option can be exercised, for 
example, a user is allowed to exercise the option up until July 31st

A quantity limit up to which exercises can be created, for example, 800 tons out of 1000 
tons can be fixed

A price reference for the non-fixed quantity can be defined (the non-fixed quantity is the 
difference between the order quantity and the total quantity of all exercises)

• A comment can be entered

The definition is typically maintained in the system when the business document, such as a 
sales contract, is created.

After the option has been defined, it is exercised in the next step of the business process: The 
business partners agree on a fixed price for the whole or for parts of the scheduled quantity. 
When this fixed price is entered in the system, the price fixation option is exercised.

Exercise details are captured within specific CPE terms, for example, an agreed fixed price of 
7000 $ / ton for 700 tons of the order quantity

Facts for Price Fixation Options

“So what's it about?"

An option to fix the price up to a certain quantity within a 
H! C A T M  ▼  - O) . •* contractually-defined timeframe is a common business practice in 

•  7M.OOO 1CV J -000.00 «*D l Ti commodity trading.

A floating price can be replaced with a fixed price for parts or for 
the whole scheduled quantity.

The option itself and the change of a floating price into a fixed price 
are reflected in risk management.

Key Pain Points Addressed

... I• OS *> r» »’ B- Price fixation options can be defined and exercised 
Integration of price fixation options with risk management

Facts 8. Figures: Key Product Features

Roles: Trader, Sales Manager, Purchase Manager
Define a price fixation option: limit quantity for fixation, period 

Target Segment: Commodity Sales, Commodity Procurement when the option can be exercised.

Planned Availability: SAP Enhancement Package 7 for SAP ERP 6.0 Exercise the price fixation option for parts or for the whole of the 
quantity, multiple exercises supported.

Use of the Configurable User Interface for Pricing, Agree on a fixed price, a fixed exchange rate or a reference 
Prerequisites: price quotations based on Derivative Contract price for a specific date.

Specifications
Multiple exercises for different components supported.

Purchasing, Sales. Global Trade Management, 
Relevant applications:

Risk Management

©  2 0 1 4  S A P  S E  o r  a n  S A P  affilia te  c o m p a n y  All r ig h ts  r e s e r v e d

Multiple exercises for different components supported

If the purchased or sold goods consist of multiple components, it is possible to agree on 
individual price fixations at component level. In this way, individual agreements for price 
fixation can be defined and exercised for each component.

For example, copper concentrate contains components like copper, silver and gold. If you 
sell copper concentrate, it is therefore possible to fix any of those components individually: 
For example, you could fix silver and gold on different days and still refer to a market price 
for copper. In addition, it is possible to create multiple exercises for price fixation for each of 
the components.

Further Facts for Price Fixation Options

Price fixation is enabled for different business processes and documents

The following documents are supported:1
• In Global Trade Management (GTM): Trading contracts and pre-contracts 

In Materials Management (MM): Purchase orders
In Sales and Distribution (SD): Inquiries, quotations, sales contracts, sales orders, invoices

A price fixation option can be defined in one document but exercised in a follow-on 
document: for example, they can be defined in a sales contract and exercised in a sales 
order.

Price fixation options are changeable unless the pricing screens are no longer editable.

1Use of the new Configurable User Interface for Pricing is mandatory

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved Internal 5

Let us assume the definition of a price fixation option is initially created in a contract. As a 
follow-on, a sales order is created and the definition for the price fixation option is copied 
automatically to that sales order. If the definition of the price fixation option is changed in the 
contract at this point, the sales order is not updated accordingly. It is then necessary to carry 
out the same change in the sales order manually.

Business Context: Purpose of Price Fixation Options

The sales and purchase of commodities are based on complex calculation rules.
Price negotiations between a buyer and seller can result in the following:
• A floating1price (market price on future dates)
• A fixed price
• A mixture of a floating and a fixed price

Typically, a floating price is defined as a starting price for the whole pricing-relevant 
quantity. A price fixation option allows you to replace the floating price either for parts or for 
the whole pricing-relevant quantity with an agreed fixed price.

Price risks for a floating price, a fixed price, and a price fixation option are considered 
differently as the existence of a price fixation option might require a different form of 
hedging.

'Various different expressions are used in commodity business, e g. unpriced, price to be fixed, non-fixed

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved. Internal 5

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

@ SAP SE AC710 339

 Visit : www.erpexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

Business Context: Definition of a Price Fixation Option

Buyer and seller agree on specific rules for a price fixation option
A price fixation option is defined at CPE term level and contains the following:

An exercise period
• A limit quantity
• A definition stating how the quantity is maintained in the exercise (by factors or absolute) and how 

the remaining quantity of the original floating term is calculated if exercises are created
A definition stating which price is applied to any quantity not covered by an exercise 
A text comment (optional), for example to describe further contractual details

Price fixation options can be defined in one document but exercised in a follow-on 
document: For example, they can be defined in a quotation and exercised in an order 

Definition and exercises of a price fixation option are only copied once
No automatic adjustment of the definition and exercises in subsequent documents after initial copy

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved Internal 6

Exercise Period
Exercises can be created within this period. The exercise period is defined by the earliest 
and the latest exercise date. For each date field, you can enter the date manually or select 
a CPE routine. The earliest exercise date is not a mandatory field. It is possible to enter just 
the latest exercise date to define the end of the exercise period.
Note: The system checks the exercise period when an exercise is created. If the check 
fails, an information message is displayed, however the user is able to continue even if the 
exercise is created outside the exercise period: the reason for this is, for example, to 
support the use case where a phone call took place on the last day of the exercise period, 
but the data is entered on the next business day. Fundamentally, price fixation options can 
be defined and exercised if the pricing screen in the transaction is editable.

Limit Quantity
The total fixed quantity of the exercises should not exceed the defined limit quantity. If the 
limit quantity is exceeded by the total quantity of all exercise terms, an information message 
is displayed.

Copying Definitions and Exercises of a Price Fixation Option
Let us assume the definition of a price fixation option is initially created in a contract. As a 
follow-on, a sales order is created and the definition for the price fixation option is copied 
automatically to that sales order. If the definition of the price fixation option is changed in 
the contract at this point, the sales order is not updated accordingly. It is then necessary to 
carry out the same change in the sales order manually. The same pattern is implemented 
for exercises of a price fixation option. If an exercise term was copied to a follow-on 
document, any change made to the same exercise term in the original document is not 
automatically reflected in the follow-on document that has already been created. For newly 
created follow-on documents, the changes made to the exercise term are reflected during 
copying.

Business Context: Exercise of the Price Fixation Option

Buyer and seller agree on a fixed price within the exercise period1
Exercises for price fixation are created by entering one of the following:
• A fixed price
• A specific date (or period) for a market price based on derivative contract specifications (DCS)
• An exchange rate
• A quantity

The system automatically calculates:
A weighted average price based on the prices for the fixed and non-fixed quantities 
The non-fixed quantity (term commodity quantity minus sum of fixations2)
The quantity for price fixation (limit quantity minus sum of fixations2)

• The price fixation status

1You can specify who is allowed to execute the option (buyer s or seller’s 
call) in the comment field for the definition of the price fixation option 

2A negative value of the calculated difference is set to zero.

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved Internal

Price Fixation Status

The price fixation status indicates whether exercises have already been created, and if the 
limit quantity has been reached by the total quantity of the exercises. The following statuses 
are set by the system:

• Not yet processed -  No exercise has been created for a price fixation option

Partially processed -  At least one exercise has been created, but the total quantity of all 
exercises does not cover the limit quantity for price fixation

Completely processed - At least one exercise has been created, and the total quantity of all 
exercises equals or exceeds the limit quantity for price fixation

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company All rights reserved Internal

A price fixation option allows the business partners to replace a floating price with an agreed 
fixed price for parts or for the whole scheduled quantity. The price fixation option consists of 
two parts: the definition and the exercises.

The definition of the price fixation option allows users to capture contractual details such as the 
following:

• An exercise period or a latest exercise date up to which the option can be exercised, for 
example, a user is allowed to exercise the option up until July 31st

A quantity limit up to which exercises can be created, for example, 800 tons out of 1000 
tons can be fixed

A price reference for the non-fixed quantity can be defined (the non-fixed quantity is the 
difference between the order quantity and the total quantity of all exercises)

• A comment can be entered

The definition is typically maintained in the system when the business document, such as a 
sales contract, is created.

After the option has been defined, it is exercised in the next step of the business process: The 
business partners agree on a fixed price for the whole or for parts of the scheduled quantity. 
When this fixed price is entered in the system, the price fixation option is exercised.

Exercise details are captured within specific CPE terms, for example, an agreed fixed price of 
7000 $ / ton for 700 tons of the order quantity

Price Fixation Process

Price fixation options are defined and exercised at CPE term level1

Definition of a price fixation option:
Typically defined for a floating term of a CPE formula 

• One definition of a price fixation option for each CPE term 
New CPE routines available to control the processing of price fixation options

Exercise of a price fixation option:
Multiple exercise terms can be created for each price fixation option 
Calculation of remaining quantity for the floating term
Net price calculation based on entered fixed prices and fixed quantities that considers the price for 
any remaining non-fixed quantity (for example, if the fixed quantity is 70 % of the scheduled 
quantity)

1Use of the new Configurable User Interface for Pricing is mandatory. 
Check the SAP Help Portal for further details on the new Ul.

It is essential to understand the quantities and the related prices throughout the price fixation 
process. In the example presented above, the order quantity of 1000 tons of copper cathodes 
in the contract is priced based on the average monthly market price for LME copper. There is a 
price fixation option defined in the contract with a limit quantity of 800 tons. Hence the buyer is 
allowed to agree with the seller on a fixed price up to this limit quantity.

Example Calculation

Contract (Definition of Price Fixation)
9 Scheduled Quantity 1000 tons @LME Copper, monthly average
* Limit Quantity 800 tons

• Quantity for Price Fixation 800 tons

Order (Exercise of Price Fixation)
9 Scheduled Quantity 1000 tons weighted average price
9 Limit Quantity 800 tons
9 Exercise Quantity (Fix1) 400 tons @9,000 $ / ton
9 Exercise Quantity (Fix2) 300 tons @8,000 $ / ton
9 Quantity for Price Fixation 100 tons (= Limit Quantity -  Total Exercise 

Quantity)
9 Non-Fixed Quantity 300 tons (= Order Quantity -  Total Exercise 

Quantity) @LME Copper, monthly average

Price Fixation Options and Risk Management I

Price fixation is reflected within Treasury and Risk Management (TRM)1

If a price fixation option is defined and exercised, raw exposure items are created to 
consider the following:
• Existence of a price fixation option

Fixed quantity with a fixed price, fixed date, or a fixed period 
Non-fixed quantity with a floating price

• Quantity above limit quantity up to term quantity (with a floating price)

Raw exposure items are converted into an exposure quantity.

A price fixation status is set for the exposure quantities.

Prerequisite: Logistics to TRM integration is enabled

CPE Routines for Price Fixation Options

New CPE routines for price fixation options
Price fixation leverages the concept of CPE routines, which are well established in the 
CPE and offer the flexibility to customize the evaluation result calculation.

Routines available for price fixation options and their purpose:
• Exercise Date Routine: Determines exercise dates automatically
• Limit Routine: Calculates or defines the limit quantity for price fixation options

Quantity Distribution Routine: Calculates the exercise quantity and the remaining non-fixed
quantity

• Reference Price Routine: Determines a price for the non-fixed quantity

SAP delivers standard CPE routine implementations, to support typical business 
requirements.

CPE Routines for Price Fixation Options
Exercise Date Routine: SAP Standard Implementations

Exercise Date Routine
Available for earliest exercise date and latest exercise date 

• Start of configured QP: Sets the date to the calculated start date of the quotation period 
End of configured QP: Sets the date to the calculated end date of the quotation period 
Manual Date Entry: The user enters the date manually 
Reference Date: The date is determined by a reference date routine

CPE Routines for Price Fixation Options
Limit Routine: SAP Standard Implementations

Limit Routine
Manually entered maximum quantity: An absolute maximum quantity is specified by the user 
Manually entered maximum percentage: A percentage is entered and the system calculates the limit 
quantity based on the actual term quantity used

CPE Routines for Price Fixation Options
Quantity Distribution Routine: SAP Standard Implementations

Quantity Distribution Routine
Proportional distribution based on factors: During creation of exercise, the quantity is entered as a 
percentage or a factor. The system calculates the exercise quantity by applying the factor to the 
used quantity of the term.
Proportional distribution based on fixed quantity: Quantity is entered but converted into factors 
internally. The system calculates the exercise quantity by applying the factor to the used quantity of 
the term.
Quantity for price fixation: The quantity is entered as an absolute quantity. It is not converted into 
factors internally and it does not change in any follow-on document.

Definition of Price Fixation Option
Exc. Date Routine Start of configured QP
Earlest Exc. Date 01.08.2013

Latest Exercise Date 31.08.2013

CPE Routines for Price Fixation Options
Reference Price Routine: SAP Standard Implementations

Reference Price Routine
• Floating price: The floating price of the term is used for the non-fixed quantity.

Weighted average of entered fixed prices: The weighted average of fixed prices is calculated and 
applied to the non-fixed quantity.
Price of last fixation: The price of the last exercise term is applied to the non-fixed quantity.

Definition of Price Fixation Option

Exercises

9
■ Unit: Price Fixation Options

• ---
• --- Lesson: Define and Exercise a Price Fixation Option
• ---

At the end of this exercise, you will be able to:

• Define a price fixation option

• Exercise the price fixation option for the whole or parts of the quantity

A company agrees with a contractual partner to allow a floating price to 
be replaced with a fixed price for parts or the whole scheduled quantity 
up until a certain date in the quotation period (QP).

1-1 Create a sales contract (contract type: Quantity Contract) to sell a commodity (for
example, a copper cathode) with a floating price based on Derivative Contract
Specification (DCS)

1-1-1 Validity Period from 1st day of next month until last day e.g. 3 month later, 
Sales organization 0001, Distribution channel 01, Sold-To Party 
CM20_CMT03

1-1-2 Enter a material (for example, CM_CU_CAT) and a target quantity (for 
example, 10000 TO)

1-2 Create a Price Fixation Option for the final term of the copper price condition

1-2-1 Set the earliest exercise date to the 2nd Friday of the 1st month of the contract’s 
validity date range

Set the latest exercise date to 2nd Monday of the 2nd month of the contract’s 
validity date range

1-2-2 Set the Limit Quantity for the price fixation to 50% (or 5000 TO) of the 
contract’s quantity

1-2-3 The quantity of the fixed and floating prices should be according to the fixed 
quantity

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

@ SAP SE AC710 373

 Visit : www.erpexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

1-3 Create a sales order with reference to the contract for 70% of the contract’s quantity 
and define the delivery date within the last week of the 1st month of the contract’s 
validity date range

1-3-1 Define a Fixation Exercise for 4000 TO of an appropriate value (for example, 
7000 USD/TO copper)

1-3-2 Check the term result based on the definition 

Note:

If no price quotations are retrieved in step 1-1 and/or step 1-3, the DCS-based market 
data are not yet available. In this case, for the quotation definition you use in the term, 
execute report ZTBA_PRICEQUOT_RANDOM with the following data:

• Keydate from: Today’s date

• Keydate to: End of this year (Caution: Do not use the default date)

• Price Date From: Start date of your quotation period

• Price Date To: Today’s date

Functionality Overview

Logistics to Treasury Integration for Commodity Risks was developed based on the 
following settings:
MM Purchase Orders:
• Item category ‘Space’, price control at ‘GR Date’, ‘GR-Based IV’ flag set, ‘Return Item’ flag NOT set, 

and subsequent process steps:
-  Raw exposure creation at goods receipt with new pricing
-  Raw exposure status update at invoice verification, based on goods receipt

SD Sales Order:
• Sales items (return flag VBAP-SHKZG = SPACE) in sales orders (SO; VBAK-VBTYP= ‘C’, VBAK- 

VBKLT = SPACE) with delivery-related billing (VBAP-FKREL= ‘A’, ‘H\ ‘J’ or ‘M’) create and update 
the raw exposure based on the confirmed item quantity, which remains open for delivery. 
Subsequent process steps:
-  Raw exposure update at outbound delivery processing (including goods issue) based on a customer invoice 

simulation
-  Raw exposure status update at customer invoice processing

Business Context 1/2

The purchasing department is responsible for the negotiation and execution of 
purchase contracts.

• Purchase contracts are outline agreements that contain special conditions 
negotiated between the purchaser and a vendor, for example, price, target value 
or target quantity. A purchase contract is valid for a specified period.

The treasury and risk department is interested in the risk relevant data of 
purchase contracts for risk reporting and hedging.

In contrast with purchase orders or scheduling agreements, contracts do not 
contain any scheduling information. Due to the lack of this data, the system 
cannot write any raw exposures.

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved. Internal

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

@ SAP SE AC710 398

 Visit : www.erpexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

Business Context 2/2

To overcome this deficit, a risk distribution plan (RDP) for quantity contracts 
has been introduced. The RDP breaks down the validity period of the contract 
into multiple short periods and assigns a partial quantity of the total quantity of 
a contract item to each of these periods.

The system is now able to write raw exposures for the quantities in the RDP 
periods with the end date of each period.

The quantities in the RDP periods are consumed by purchase orders created 
with reference to the contract.

Note:

RDPs are only used for writing raw exposures. They are not used 
in any logistics processes.

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved. Internal

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

@ SAP SE AC710 399

 Visit : www.erpexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

RDP in Quantity Contracts

When processing a contract item, you can display the RDP information by choosing 
the following path from the menu:
Goto Item —>More —>Risk Distribution Plan

The RDP screen contains the 
following information:

• The validity period and the 
target quantity of the current 
contract item and whether a 
distribution strategy is 
assigned (1)

• How the quantity is distributed
(2)

Updating Raw Exposures

To update a raw exposure, you use the end date of the RDP period and the Open 
Risk Quantity.
The Open Risk Quantity is the difference between the quantity that was originally 
planned for this period and the quantity that was ordered with reference to this 
contract item.

Consumption of RDPs

When a contract is created or changed, the Planned Risk Quantity is maintained 
for each RDP period.

• When a purchase order is created with reference to the contract at a later time, 
the delivery date of the purchase order item is used to determine the RDP period 
in the contract. The quantity of the purchase order item is added to the Ordered 
Quantity in the affected RDP period.
The Open Risk Quantity is calculated as the difference between the Planned 
Risk Quantity and the Ordered Quantity.

Risk Distribution Strategy

The strategy enables you to automatically distribute the target quantity of a contract 
item to time periods within the validity period of the contract.
SAP delivers an example strategy. This strategy creates monthly periods with a 
maximum planning horizon of 2 years. The target quantity of the contract item is 
distributed on a daily basis.

Example:
A contract has a validity period of 10 years.
The item has a target quantity of 10000 tons.

Result:
Initially, the RDP will consist of 24 periods (covering the first 2 years) and 
2000 tons will be assigned to the existing periods.
Months with 31 days will be assigned more than months with 30 days

Automatic RDP Update (AutoUpdate)

If you set the Automatic RDP Update for a contract item, the RDP will be updated 
whenever the contract is changed.
This covers the creation of new RDP periods as well as the adjustment of the 
planned risk quantity if the consumption has been higher or lower for past periods.

Examples:

1: If an RDP has been created with a planning horizon of 2 years, and 
after half a year the contract is changed (or transaction LITRMS1is run), 
6 new periods will be created.

2: An RDP consists of 10 periods, each period has 100 tons. 5 periods 
have now passed, but only 400 tons have been ordered. If the 
AutoUpdate is performed at this point, the open quantity of 600 tons is 
assigned to the 5 open/future periods.

Business Context

Purchase orders with goods listed at stock exchanges contain a price risk. This is 
either a risk about a price agreement which references a floating market price or a 
risk about an agreed fix price because the market price changes over time.

With the logistic-to-treasury integration relevant information about the price risk is 
sent automatically and in time to the treasury and risk management (TRM). A raw 
exposure in TRM is created for every price risk in the purchase order. Two 
possibilities exist:

Raw Exposure at Item Level
Raw exposures are sent to TRM based on purchase order item level. Even if there 
are multiple schedule lines, only the sum of the ordered quantity is sent to TRM.

Raw Exposure at Schedule Line Level
To get more precise risk-relevant data, raw exposures consider planned delivery 
information in schedule lines: Ordered quantities on planned delivery dates.

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved. Internal

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

Raw Exposure Items at Schedule Line Level: 
Comparison with Item Level

This slide illustrates the different granularity of a raw exposure from a purchase order item.

The raw exposure represents the risk from a floating price agreement. The following settings are 
made:

A risk-relevant final CPE term considers the market prices in a quotation period “one month 
after goods receipt”.

♦ “Goods-Receipt-Based Invoice Verification” is active.

Price determination occurs on the date of goods receipt.

The pure commodity material has the same quantity unit of measure in the document and in 
the raw exposure.
No payable- and item adjustment condition.

According to these settings, the price determination of the purchase order item is based on the 
entire quantity 250 TO on the delivery date specified in the first schedule line 16.06.2013. This 
result is persisted in the document database.

Raw exposure determination for the purchase order item depends on the granularity level:

For granularity at schedule line level, two raw exposure items have been created:

1. 100 TO, quotation period July, Due Date 31.07.2013

2. 150 TO, quotation period August, Due Date 31.08.2013

With individual price simulations for every schedule line.

Where the raw exposure information is determined with the scheduled quantities and 
dates.

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

@ SAP SE AC710 419

 Visit : www.erpexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

In this example, the quotation periods are calculated with CPE reference date = goods receipt 
pricing date.

Note that only CPE reference dates that refer to the schedule line delivery date result in 
quotation periods that fit the scheduled dates.

• For granularity at item level, one raw exposure item has been created:

1. 250 TO, quotation period July, Due Date 31.07.2013

The raw exposure information is determined with the order item price determination 
result.

No price simulation takes place.

The goods receipt takes place as planned in the delivery schedule lines.

• Two raw exposures have been created with different information:

1. 100 TO, quotation period July, Due Date 31.07.2013

2. 150 TO, quotation period August, Due Date 31.08.2013

With individual price determination at each goods receipt.

Where the raw exposure information is determined with the goods receipt dates and 
quantities that fit the scheduled quantities and dates.

In this example, the accuracy of the raw exposure items used to represent the price risk in TRM 
is significantly higher right from the start, when granularity at schedule line level is used.

Raw Exposure Items at Schedule Line Level: Risk Data

1. Once a PO is created, a raw exposure item exists for every schedule line. Each item has a 
Quantity calculated from the scheduled quantity, and Due Date calculated from the 
scheduled delivery date. If GR takes place with the planned quantities on the planned 
dates, the accuracy of the PO risk data is improved compared to the risk data at item level.

Raw Exposures: Overview

97650 0300000002000200000 PORD 4500007905000010 YP2C TST2 COPPER 150 TO 31.08.2013

2. After posting GRs with the planned quantities on the planned dates, the GR raw exposure 
items take over the risk with identical quantities and dates.

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved. Internal 9

1. At this point in time, the purchase order has been saved.
Raw exposure from the purchase order has been created with ID 97650.
The purchase order raw exposure has been determined with granularity at schedule line level: 

Two raw exposures have been determined with schedule-line-individual price simulations:
- For the first schedule line:

Risk quantity 100 TO for the scheduled quantity.
Quotation period July is determined from the scheduled delivery date “one month after 
goods receipt”.
Due Date 31.07.2013 is the last date in the quotation period.
For the second schedule line:
Risk quantity 150 TO for the scheduled quantity.
Quotation period August is determined from the scheduled delivery date “one month after 
goods receipt”.
Due Date 31.08.2013 is the last date in the quotation period.

2. At this point in time, the two goods receipts have been posted as planned in the delivery 
schedule.
Raw exposures from the goods receipts have been created with the IDs 97651 and 97652.
• Every goods receipt creates an individual raw exposure.

Price calculation takes place for every goods receipt considering the goods receipt posting 
date and goods receipt quantity.
The individual pricing result is persisted in the database and leads to individual raw 
exposures.

 Visit : www.erpexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

Conclusion:

Granularity at schedule line level produces an accurate raw exposure at the beginning of the 
purchase.

■  This improvement in accuracy is useful when:

* Multiple schedule lines exist

* Goods receipts are posted as planned in the delivery schedule

* The quotation period depends on the scheduled dates.

This improvement in accuracy requires an additional price simulation for raw exposure.

Example at Item Level

1. Once a PO is created, a raw exposure item exists for the purchase order item. It has a 
Quantity calculated from the item quantity, and Due Date calculated from the item price 
date. The planned delivery information in the schedule lines is not considered. For this 
reason, the quantities of the PO and GR raw exposures differ for each due date and

items take over the risk from the PO and calculate it again using the GR quantities and 
dates.

The second example purchase order 4500007908 has been created using the same document 
data as in the first purchase order.

a) Delivery schedule line 1 with 100 TO on delivery date 16.06.2013

b) Delivery schedule line 2 with 150 TO on delivery date 17.07.2013

Two goods receipts have been created using the same data as in the first example process:

a) GR 5000007434 with 100 TO on 16.06.2013

b) GR 5000007435 with 150 TO on 17.07.2013

1. At this point in time, the purchase order has been saved.

Raw exposure from the purchase order has been created with ID 97653.

Unlike in the first example purchase order, this raw exposure has been determined with 
granularity at item level:

One raw exposure for the purchase order item has been determined from the price calculation 
result.
Risk quantity 250 TO for the entire document item quantity.

Quotation period July is determined from the delivery date of the first schedule line “one month 
after goods receipt”.

• Due Date 31.07.2013 is the last date in the quotation period.

2. At this point in time, the two goods receipts have been posted as planned in the delivery 
schedule.

Raw exposures from the goods receipts have been created with the IDs 97654 and 97655.

• Every goods receipt creates an individual raw exposure.

Price calculation takes place for every goods receipt considering the goods receipt posting 
date and goods receipt quantity.

The individual pricing result is persisted in the database and leads to individual raw 
exposures.

Conclusion:

Granularity at item level produces a less accurate raw exposure until the last goods receipt has 
been posted.

■  No additional price simulation for the raw exposure is carried out.

■  The improvement in accuracy will be reduced or even non-existent when:

The goods receipts deviate from the delivery schedule

• Only one schedule line exists

• The quotation period does not depend on the scheduled dates.

Raw Exposure Items at Schedule Line Level from CPE

To consider different scheduled delivery dates in the raw exposure, only certain CPE Term 
Reference Date Routines are usable:

Item Pricing Date, Document Pricing Date 
Goods Receipt Pricing Date 
Goods Receipt Posting Date 
Goods Receipt Current Date

All other routines do not consider the scheduled delivery dates but use PO item dates instead, 
meaning the dates are then identical to those in the raw exposure items from a PO item.

Configuring the Level of Raw Exposure Items:
Customizing

In Customizing, configure whether the raw exposure items are created at item level or 
schedule line level by using the following path in transaction SPRO:
SAP Reference IMG -> Logistics -  General -> Treasury and Risk Management Integration -> 
Materials Management Settings -> Purchase Order Settings -> Define Exposure Update for 
Purchase Orders

Change View "Define Raw-Exposure Update for Purchase Orders": Details

i© 0
Oefine Raw-Exposure Update for Purchase Orders_________________________________

Item Level

J® Schedule Lne Level

After changing the level, the new settings only apply to raw exposures relating to PO and GR 
documents that are changed or created from that point in time. You can use transaction 
LITRMS or the revaluation function to adapt existing raw exposures.

Configuring the Level of Raw Exposure Items:
Customer BAdl

If you need a more flexible approach for controlling the level of raw exposure items, the 
following customer BAdl method is available, which enables you to set the level for every 
purchase order item individually:

• BADI definition LOG_TRM_UPDATE_EXPOSURE_CUST

• Interface IF_BADI_LOG_TRM_UPD_EXP_CUST method 
CONTROL_RAW_EXPOSURE_ITEM_DET

For every document item, you can set the value of the changing parameter structure 
CS_DETERMINE_EXPOSURE field RE_LEVEL to fit your needs:

Value = ‘1’ -  Raw Exposure Update at Item Level (SAP standard behavior)

Value = ‘2’ -  Raw Exposure Update at Schedule Line Level

is purchased in Copper Concentrate. The Copper Concentrate is priced 
based on LME futures.

The formula which is calculating the price of the Copper content has been 
prepared in a previous task (former exercise)

1-8 Check if raw exposures have been created accordingly

What is the exposure origin key: Solution: Start transaction FTREX2, search for 
exposures using selection criteria “Entered By” (= your login user) and “Entered On” 
(= today’s date).
The exposure origin is PORD.
How many sub raw exposures exist for the order item: Solution: around 20, depending 
on the working day of the respective month when the purchase order is to be paid.
Why is that? Solution: The payment is based on a monthly average. The average is 
calculated by splitting the order item quantity over all working days of the stock 
exchange in the respective month.

Business Context

Treasury departments often manage exposures for their entire enterprise. Thus, 
STOs in general are, as a ‘left-hand <-» right-hand- process not relevant for risk 
integration

However, for reporting reasons, the ability to report the exposure view based on 
a company code is important, therefore both risk sides of a CC STO shall be 
captured as exposures in TRM.

Further, it may be the case that specific processes require Risk Management for 
one company code only. Therefore, you should be able to configure which risk 
side you want to write exposures for.

Commodity price exposure determination relies on pricing. As there is no 
independent pricing’ for CC STOs on the sales side, an independent sales 
exposure determination is not possible. However, billing on the sales side use 
the purchasing pricing of the CC STO. Thus the exposure will be mirrored.

The gold boxes describe the exposure integration for the purchasing side of a CC STO as it is in 
CM1.0. The blue boxes describes the additional mirrored exposure for the sales side in CC STO 
case

Business Context

Physical commodity stock can constitute a commodity price risk (exposure). For example, if you 
sell from stock using market prices, you may lose money if the market price goes down.

Therefore, commodity stock quantity is a relevant piece of information for updating raw exposures 
in SAP Treasury & Risk Management (TRM).

Exposures based on physical stock are closely linked with exposures based on sales or purchasing 
orders. Together they provide a complete view of your overall commodity price risk.

Commodities can be pure materials or ingredients in batch-managed materials. For batch- 
managed materials, the system uses the characteristic values to determine the exposure quantity.

Every goods movement causes a change in stock quantity and - when configured - a change in the 
corresponding material stock raw exposure. In order to keep exposures up-to-date at all times, the 
stock exposure update is integrated in all transactions that change stock quantities.

In addition a report is provided for periodic updates.

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved. Internal

Material Stock Raw Exposure, Item Data

The exposure due date is always infinity: 31.12.9999

The commodity is the physical commodity assigned to the characteristic or to the material

The quantity reflects the physical commodity stock quantity in the stock part, which is described 
by the external document number

It does not contain any index or exchange information

It does not contain any quotation period information

Exercise

9
■ Unit: Goods Receipt -  Integration with Risk Management

• ---
• --- Lesson: Post goods receipt and transfer risk relevant data 
• --- to risk management

At the end of this exercise, you will be able to do the following:

• Understand how a goods receipt affects the risk situation

• Check the generated raw exposures

A company needs aluminum sheets for its production process. Aluminum 
is purchased in aluminum sheets which contain 97 % of aluminum. The 
aluminum is priced based on LME futures.

The formula which is calculating the price of the aluminum content has 
been prepared in a previous task and a purchase order has been issued 
(former exercises)

Now the goods have arrived and a goods receipt is to be posted.

1-1 Post goods receipt to the purchase order created in the previous exercise.
Solution: Start transaction MIGO, select a “Goods Receipt” posting for “Purchase 
Order”. Movement type shall be “101”. Enter the purchase order number from the 
previous exercise. Tick the check box for “Item OK”. Push the “Check” button -  
everything should be okay. Then push button “Post”. (The system will create a batch lot 
for the posting, this is okay)

Document number:_________________

1-2 Check if raw exposure for the goods receipt has been created accordingly

Solution: Start traasaction FTREX2, search for exposures using selection criteria 
“Entered By” (= your login user) and “Entered On” (= today’s date).

What is the exposure origin key of the goods receipt:_________

Is the exposure fixed or floating:_____________
Why is that?__________________________________________________

Solution

Unit: Goods Receipt -  Integration with Risk Management
Lesson: Post goods receipt and transfer risk relevant data 
to risk management

1-1 Post goods receipt to the purchase order created in the previous exercise.

Solution: Start transaction MIGO, select a “Goods Receipt” posting for “Purchase 
Order”. Movement type shall be “101”. Enter the purchase order number from the 
previous exercise. Tick the check box for “Item OK”. Push the “Check” button -  
everything should be okay. Then push button “Post”. (The system will create a batch lot 
for the posting, this is okay)
Document number:_________________

1-2 Check if raw exposure for the goods receipt has been created accordingly

Solution: Start transaction FTREX2, search for exposures using selection criteria 
“Entered By” (= your login user) and “Entered On” (= today’s date).

What is the exposure origin key of the goods receipt: MMGR

Is the exposure fixed or floating: Floating

Why is that? Solution: The received goods are not paid yet and their value is still 
depending on the market data of the London Metal Exchange.

1-3 Check the raw exposures created during the purchase order creation.

What has been changed: Solution: The quantity has been reduced to zero and it has 
been switched from floating to fixed.

Why: Solution: The exposure has been handed over to the stock. If there were still an 
exposure on the purchase order the total exposure would be too big.

Solution

Unit: Invoice Verification
Lesson: Post invoice verification with commodity 
management

1-1 Post a provisional invoice to the purchase order created in the previous exercise.

Solution: Start transaction MIRO. Choose invoice transaction provisional and set 
differential posing to “As Invoice”. Enter today’s date as invoice date, mark “Calculate 
tax” and enter the purchase order number from the previous exercise. Push enter. Copy 
the balance value into the “Amount” in order to bring the balance to zero. Save.

Document number:_________________

1-2 Assume that some data have changed. This could be the product quality, new rates from 
the stock exchange or other parameters which can influence the commodity pricing. 
Simulate this by changing the payable copper condition type Y%CU in the purchase 
order.

Which effect can be expected in a differential invoice:____________________

Solution: In case of increasing the payable copper percentage, a differential invoice 
Start transaction MIRO. Choose invoice transaction provisional and set differential 
posing to “As Invoice”. Enter today’s date as invoice date, mark “Calculate tax” and 
enter the purchase order number from the previous exercise. Push enter. Copy the 
balance value into the “Amount” in order to bring the balance to zero (do not copy the 
minus sign)
Save.

1-3 Post a differential invoice.

Solution: Proceed the same way as before. Note that now only the difference between 
the current value and the previous value is invoiced.

Differential amount:_________________

Document number:__________________

Business Context 1/2

The sales department is responsible for the negotiation and execution of sales 
contracts.

Sales contracts are outline agreements that contain special conditions negotiated 
between the vendor and a customer, for example, price, target value or target 
quantity. A sales contract is valid for a specified period.

The treasury and risk department is interested in the risk-relevant data of sales 
contracts for risk reporting and hedging.

In contrast with sales orders or scheduling agreements, contracts do not contain 
any scheduling information. Due to the lack of this data, the system cannot write 
any raw exposures.

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved. Internal

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

@ SAP SE AC710 490

 Visit : www.erpexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

Business Context 2/2

To overcome this deficit, a risk distribution plan (RDP) for quantity contracts 
has been introduced. The RDP breaks down the validity period of the contract 
into multiple short periods and assigns a partial quantity of the total quantity of a 
contract item to each of these periods.

The system is now able to write raw exposures for the quantities in the RDP 
periods with the end date of each period.

The quantities in the RDP periods are consumed by sales orders created with 
reference to the contract.

Note:

RDPs are only used for writing raw exposures. They are not used 
in any logistics processes.

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved. Internal

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

Risk Distribution Strategy

The strategy enables you to automatically distribute the target quantity of a contract 
item to time periods within the validity period of the contract.
SAP delivers an example strategy. This strategy creates monthly periods with a 
maximum planning horizon of 2 years. The target quantity of the contract item is 
distributed on a daily basis.

Example:
A contract has a valid ity period of 10 years.

The item has a target quantity o f 10000 tons.

Result:
Initially, the RDP will consist of 24 periods (covering the firs t 2 years) and 2000 tons will 

be assigned to the existing periods.

Months with 31 days will be assigned more than months with 30 days.

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved. Internal 12

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

@ SAP SE AC710 498

 Visit : www.erpexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

Definition of a Risk Distribution Strategy

SAP delivers an example distribution 
strategy, however you can also define 
your own strategies.

To do so, implement an ABAP class 
implementing the interface 
IF_LOGTRM_RSIK_DISTR_STRAT, 
or create a class that inherits from 
class
CL_LOG_TRM_RDP_EQUAL_DISTR 
(which is the example strategy 
provided by SAP).

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved. Internal 13

If you set the Automatic RDP Update for a contract item, the RDP will be updated whenever the 
contract is changed.

This covers the creation of new RDP periods as well as the adjustment of the planned risk 
quantity if the consumption has been higher or lower for past periods.

Use C ase l:
A shipper or logistics service provider who uses SAP Transportation Management specifies a 
Freight Agreement RFQ (see Strategic Freight Procurement Process). Subsequently, the shipper 
or LSP sends the freight agreement RFQ to the carrier. The system displays the freight 
agreement RFQ as a forwarding agreement quotation in the carrier's TM system. Subsequently, 
the carrier can strategically specify rates for the items and send it to the shipper.
The shipper or LSP can also provide the RFQ information via B2B Capability (then the SAP 
Exchange Infrastructure would need to translate it in order to create a TM Forwarding Agreement 
Quotation) or Excel Sheet in an e-mail (this would have to be translated manually into SAP TM).

SD Differential Invoice

• Re-price at invoicing
• Invoice Types: Provisional / Differential and Final Invoice
• Differential Invoice has 2 items:

-  + $ amount to be invoiced
—  $ amount already invoiced

• Consider previous invoices for the remaining amount to be invoiced
• Order and Delivery related billing
• Cancellation of invoices
• Integration into VF01 (SAP Billing)
• Billing status on order or delivery document (non / partially / fully invoiced)
• Finalization depends on final quantity, price and quality
• Strong integration into CPE via conditions & status (provisional vs. final)
• Non-Final Invoices can be posted to “deferred revenue” account through account 

determination

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved. Internal

These are the main new functions provided by the concept of provisional / differential / final 
invoice.

This is a quick walkthrough.

First a Sales Order is created. The Net Value, i.e. the price, can be analysed in the pricing 
condition screen of the SO item. In this case the commodity price comes from CPE (Commodity 
Pricing Engine), by calculating a formula for the provisional price.

Flat view can be entered for the entire document or for selected FWAQ items
only

R at ProN t FlATVtEVW

Serm aton Date te E O

©  2 0 1 5  S A P S E  o r a n  S A P  affiliate c o m p a n y  All r ig h ts  re se rv e d Internal

You can enter the flat view for the entire FWAQ document or for selected items only. For entering 
the flat view for the entire document, choose the „Display Flat View" button in the global toolbar 
of the document. For entering the flat view for selected items only, choose the button with the 
same label on top of the item list.

When entering the flat view Ul you need to choose a flat view profile which we will take a look at 
later on. A default flat view profile can be assigned to the FWAQ type in customizing. A 
mandatory entry for the flat view is the simulation date. The simulation date defines the date for 
which the rates should be displayed, this means if rate tables have multiple validity periods the 
simulation date defines which rate table values should be displayed in the flat view (i.e. the 
values of the validity period in which the simulation date is).

Additionally to the simulation date the user can also define further filter criteria. The F4 help for 
these filter criteria only provide values which are used in the rate tables shown in the flat view. 
Filter criteria are not mandatory. When not using the filter criteria, all rate table values and scale 
item combinations are shown.

Please note that for performance reasons the maximum number of entries can be limited in 
customizing using IMG path SAP Transportation Management -> Transportation Management -> 
Basic Functions -> General Settings -> Define General Settings for SAP TM. In this Customizing 
activity you can define a rate table filter and a maximum number of hits which defines the 
maximum number of lines shown in the flat view. If the number of lines for the flat view exceeds 
the threshold set in Customizing it will be mandatory for the user to define filter criteria.

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

0  Visit : www.5e2r4pexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

* Received excel file has to be stored first and then uploaded into TM

Two starting points are possible, the process can start at shipper side but also start on carrier 
side, in case of updating/extending an existing contract or a selling campaign.

Input for the creation of the Forwarding Agreement Quotation can be:
• Origin/Dest Locations & Ports
• Commodity/ Equipment
• Default Route
• Capacities
• Preconditions

Input for suggesting rates/services can be:
Selling Price 
Apply Margin /Discounts 
Existing Similar Agreement 
Additional Services/Additional Cost 
Demand and Revenue History

Currently it is only possible to send the one Forwarding Agreement Quotation to one customer.

Business Context

When negotiating the contract, counterparties can agree to estimate the value at 
the beginning based on available information and to adjust it when accurate 
information becomes available. This means that logistics documents can contain 
items with unfixed prices, changeable on a periodic basis. Such variable prices are 
also known as floating prices1.

There is a need for some roles in companies (like risk and credit management) to 
know the updated value of documents with floating prices. The function 
“Revaluation of Logistics Documents" fulfills this requirement.

'T h e re  are different expressions used in com m odity business, e  g. un-priced, price to be fixed, non-fixed

© 2014 SAP SE or an SAP affiliate company. All rights reserved. Internal

For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

@ SAP SE AC710 532

 Visit : www.erpexams.com



For Any SAP / IBM / Oracle - Materials Purchase Visit : www.erpexams.com OR Contact Via Email Directly At : sapmaterials4u@gmail.com

Introduction

Floating prices are technically defined in the pricing conditions of logistics 
documents. Their estimated values change daily, and they are usually uploaded into 
the system each day as prices change.

Revaluation of Logistics Documents (transaction CMM_LREV) allows you to 
perform a new pricing to keep the price values up-to-date, in accordance with 
underlying price changes or price estimate changes. This includes subsequent 
value updates of follow-on documents, such as deliveries or goods receipts.

Note:
Because purchase contracts contain master conditions instead of document 
conditions, a special logic is implemented for these. The report only updates the 
risk distribution plans (RDPs) and sends the raw exposure to Treasury and Risk 
Management (TRM). The values of the raw exposures are based on a price 
simulation.

Report Mode

Following parameters are available in section Report Mode_________________________
V Display Results 

“Report Mode” of the selection screen: Smutation Run (No Postngs)
• Display Results Log Errors Only

Max. Number of Paralel Jobs 1
If you select this checkbox, the report displays a results 
screen showing all processed documents.

• Simulation Run (No Postings)
If you select the Simulation Run (No Postings) checkbox, the 
system runs the report and displays the results without posting 
anything to the database.

• Log Errors Only
If you select this checkbox, the report stores only error 
messages in the application log. Otherwise information and 
warning messages are stored, too.

• Max. Number of Parallel Jobs
You can use this parameter to speed up the processing time. 
The entered number is used to optimize the number of parallel 
jobs that are started by the report to revaluate the documents.

Error Handling

Reprocessng Errors
Items with Errors Ont/ 

Run Timestamp to

To reprocess items with errors, you can use the following parameters on the selection screen 
of the revaluation report:

Items with Errors Only. If this checkbox is selected, the report processes only items that 
have been processed before, but have not been completed successfully due to an error.

Run Timestamp-. Whenever you run the report, the start date and time of the run are 
stored. You can select this date and time if you want to process all documents from a 
specific run (for example if certain market data was not uploaded correctly).

Business Context

Commodities often have index-based floating prices, that is, the final price 
may only be known some periods after goods receipt / goods issue.

In physical contracts, revenue and costs are first recognized based on the provisional 
price at the date of fulfillment, that is, goods issue / goods receipt.

Adjustments to the sale / purchase price are made subsequently based on movements 
in quoted market up to the date of final pricing (differential invoicing, differential billing).

The fair value of the final price adjustment needs to be revalued
continuously and changes in its value are recognized as an
adjustment to revenue or cost through the profit & loss (P/L) at period-end.

It is common business practice to determine the final price adjustment based on 
reference to forward market prices. ( Mt OlfW W  *•.»«-»

Period-end valuation has to be done in sales and purchasing.

iM M na

Benefits

• Error-prone manual calculation of accruals is completely automated.

Time-sensitive calculation of accruals is decoupled from the actual postings and 
can be done overnight.

• Process control is supported via approval process.

• Approval process for postings is via workflow possible.

• Completeness of PEV activities is ensured by the following:

Automatic determination of relevant logistics documents

A completeness check that ensures that all
relevant logistics documents have been considered in PEV

Recap: Trading contract, definition and purpose

The trading contract:
Is the leading document of Global Trade Management (GTM) 
Integrates multiple legal contracts between customers and vendors
Is used to maintain sales orders and purchase orders in a single 
transaction

Trading Contract
Purchasing

JJ

© 2014 SAP SE o r  a n  SAP affilia te co m p a n y  All n g h ts  re se rv e d .

Trading contracts are documents in the SAP system that integrate multiple legal contracts 
between customers and vendors. With the trading contract, both sales orders and purchase 
orders can be maintained using a single transaction.

Overview
Oil & Gas enhanced CM Processes

■  Commodity Management Processes

The integrated Commodity Management (CM) solution provides customers a platform to 
manage the end to end process of buying and selling commodities, risk management, 
transportation and financial settlement/hedge management. The ultimate value is higher 
transparency on risk exposures leading to better decision making, lower risk, more effective 
hedging as well logistics processes.

IS-Oil Enhancements for Commodity Management

For Oil & Gas customers a compatibility of Commodity Management features with IS-OIL 
enhancements in SD and MM is provided. Especially, the oil-specific quantity conversion 
interface (QCI) is considered in the commodity pricing engine (CPE) and the SD differential 
invoicing.

■  New IS-OIL Functions
In addition, an Authority to Load -  Credit Check is provided and the TSW Nomination is 
integrated smoothly with Global Trade Management (GTM) via an enhanced TSW reference 
document update. This lowers the risks for bulk commodity shipments and improves the 
integration of trading and scheduling.

■  Comment on Slide

The shown CM process overview is only a possible variant. There are also other CM process 
variants possible with IS-OIL (for example, using SD/MM processes without GTM and without 
TSW Bulk Scheduling).

Fuel supply chain management overview

SAP Fuel Supply Chain Management for 
Fuel Supply Chain Utilities provides the ability to:

Management
Manage fossil fuels like coal, natural gas and 
liquid fuel

Fuel Procurement Give detailed insights into the fuel cost structure 
of conventional power production

Fuel Inventory Management • Integrate the fuel procurement process into SAP 
ERP while adding fuel specific functionality

Fuel Transportation Plan and schedule the supply of fuels over 
different transport channels

• Support of the entire Quality Management 
Quality Management process in the supply chain

Commodity Risk • Manage financial risks related to fuel 
Management procurement
